Purity of Flowing Water and Large Cisterns
Ruling on purity of flowing water and large cisterns

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for flowing water and large cisterns when impurity falls into them and identify the condition that keeps the water pure.

Core Idea
Flowing water and large cisterns remain pure until a trace of impurity appears.

This lesson covers a key principle in taharah: flowing water and large cisterns are not automatically impure when najasah enters. Instead, they remain pure as long as no trace (color, taste, smell) of the impurity is visible. This principle is essential for everyday wudu in natural water sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the water type
Determine whether the water is flowing (stream, river) or a large cistern (ghadeer 'adheem) that moves when one side is disturbed.
If it is a small stagnant pool, a different ruling applies.
2
Check for visible trace of impurity
Look for any change in color, taste, or smell caused by the impurity. If none is found, the water remains pure.
The trace must be apparent; microscopic or hypothetical traces are not considered.
3
Apply the ruling
If no trace is visible, wudu is permissible from any part of the water. For a large cistern, only the side where impurity fell requires caution.
The impurity is considered localized due to the volume and movement of water.
4
Identify when water becomes impure
If a trace of impurity appears (e.g., color, taste, smell), the water becomes impure and cannot be used for purification.
This applies to both flowing water and large cisterns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واما الماء الجاري اذا وقعت فيه نجاسة جاز الوضوء منه اذا لم ير لها اثر لانها لا تستقر مع جريان الماء والغدير العظيم الذي اذا حركت جنبة يتحرك الاخر جاز الوضوء من جانبه الاخر اذا كانت النجاسة في احد الجانبين
As for flowing water, when impurity falls into it, wudu from it is permissible if no trace of it is visible because the impurity does not settle due to the flowing of water. And a large cistern such that when one side is moved the other side moves, it is permissible to perform wudu from its other side if the impurity is on one side.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings: (1) Flowing water (maa' jaari) remains pure if najasah falls into it, provided there is no visible trace (color, taste, smell) of the impurity. This is because the flowing water carries away the impurity, preventing it from settling. (2) A large cistern (ghadeer 'adheem) that is so large that disturbing one side causes the other side to move—if najasah falls in one part, the other part remains pure and can be used for wudu. This is because the water is effectively like flowing water; the impurity is localized and does not reach the other side due to the large volume and movement.

Key Terms
ماء جاري (maa' jaari): Flowing water that moves continuously, such as a stream, river, or canal water that is not stagnant.
غدير عظيم (ghadeer 'adheem): A large cistern or pond where disturbing one side causes the other side to move; typically more than 10x10 cubits or a large body of standing water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a dead bird falls into a large cistern (ghadeer 'adheem) on one side, can a person perform wudu from the opposite side according to the Hanafi school?
A) No, because the entire cistern becomes impure.
B) Yes, as long as no trace of impurity (color, taste, smell) appears on the opposite side.
C) Only if the bird is not a dog or pig.
D) No, because the water is standing and thus becomes impure entirely.

Key Takeaway
Flowing water and large cisterns are presumed pure until a visible trace of impurity appears.

Flowing Water and Impurity: The Trace Condition
Ruling on flowing water with impurity and its proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on flowing water when impurity falls, identify the condition that triggers impurity, and explain the proof from the hadith of Abu Umamah.

Core Idea
Flowing water remains pure unless its color, taste, or smell changes—impurity does not settle.

A common scenario: impurity falls into a flowing river or stream. Does the water become impure immediately? The Hanafi school provides a clear, practical ruling based on observable change. This lesson unpacks that ruling, its condition, and the prophetic proof underlying it. Understanding this will prevent unnecessary hardship and clarify the role of flowing water in purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The passage rules on 'flowing water when impurity falls into it.' What is the default hukm? The author says 'it is permissible to perform ablution from it' if no trace is seen. So the act is using flowing water for wudu after impurity falls, and the ruling is that it remains permissible (the water is pure).
Ruling is permissibility, not absolute purity without condition.
2
Locate the Condition for Impurity
The water becomes impure only if 'a trace' (اثر) of the impurity appears. The commentary clarifies that 'trace' refers to change in color, taste, or smell. If none of these three qualities change, the water stays pure.
Trace = change in one of the awsaf thalatha.
3
Examine the Legal Reasoning ('Illah)
Why does flow matter? Because impurity does not settle in moving water; it is carried away. Therefore, the water at the point of use remains unaffected. This is a special dispensation for flowing water.
Compare to standing water where impurity may mix thoroughly.
4
Analyze the Prophetic Proof (Dalil)
The hadith from Abu Umamah states: 'Water is not made impure by anything except what overcomes its smell, taste, and color.' This directly supports the ruling: impurity is only effective when it changes the water's qualities. The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalala).
The wording 'لا ينجسه شيء' is general, but the exception makes the condition explicit.
5
Note the Inter-Madhhab Perspective
Imam al-Shafi'i uses a quantity-based approach (two qullahs) for all water, whether flowing or not. The Hanafi school prioritizes flow over volume, but both schools agree that a change in qualities indicates impurity. The practical difference arises for small flowing amounts.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واما الماء الجاري اذا وقعت فيه نجاسة جاز الوضوء منه اذا لم يرلها اثر لانها لاتستقر مع جريان الماء (۳۹) اور جاری پانی جب کہ اس میں نجاست گر جائے پھر بھی اس سے وضو جائز ہے اگر اس میں نجاست کا کوئی اثر نظر نہ آئے ۔ اس لئے کہ نا پا کی پانی بہنے کی وجہ سے ٹھہرے گی نہیں۔ تشریح نجاست کا اثر نظر نہ آنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نجاست کی وجہ سے پانی کا رنگ یا بو یا مزا میں سے ایک بدل جائے تو جاری پانی ہونے کے با وجود اس سے وضو یا غسل کرنا جائز نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر نا پا کی گری لیکن پانی کا مزایا بو یا رنگ ناپاکی گرنے کی وجہ سے نہیں بدلا تو اس پانی سے وضو یا غسل کرنا جائز ہے۔ وہ پانی ابھی تک پاک ہے۔ (1) اس لئے کہ جیسے ہی ناپا کی گری تو اس کو جاری پانی بہا کر دوسری جگہ لے گیا وہاں ٹھہر نے نہیں دیا۔ اس لئے اس جگہ کا پانی پاک رہا (2) حدیث میں ہے کہ ماء کثیر کا جب تک رنگ، بو اور مزا نہ بدلے پاک ہے عن ابی امامه الباهلي قال قال رسول الله له ان الماء لا ينجسه شيء الا ما غلب على ريحه وطعمه ولونه (ب) (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب الحیاض، ص 74 ، نمبر 21 5 طحاوی، باب الماء وتقع فيه النجاسة ص 15) مسئلہ نمبر 37 پر حدیث قلتین گزری اس سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ماہ کثیر میں ناپاکی گرنے سے ناپاک نہیں ہو گا جب تک کہ اوصاف ثلاثہ میں سے ایک نہ بدل جائے۔
And as for flowing water, when impurity falls into it, it is permissible to perform ablution from it if no trace of it is seen, because it does not settle due to the flow of water. (39) And flowing water: when impurity falls into it, still ablution from it is permissible if no effect of the impurity is seen. Because impurity does not settle due to the flow. Explanation: The meaning of 'no effect seen' is that if due to impurity one of the water's color, smell, or taste changes, then despite being flowing water, ablution or ritual bath from it is not permissible. But if impurity falls but the water's taste, smell, or color does not change due the impurity, then ablution or ritual bath from it is permissible. That water is still pure. (1) Because as soon as impurity falls, the flowing water sweeps it away to another place and does not let it settle. Therefore the water at that spot remains pure. (2) There is a hadith that large water (al-ma' al-kathir) is pure as long as its color, smell, and taste do not change: from Abu Umamah al-Bahili that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Water is not made impure by anything except what overcomes its smell, taste, and color.' (Ibn Majah) The hadith of qullatayn has passed under issue 37; from it also it is known that large water does not become impure by impurity falling unless one of the three qualities changes.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on flowing water when impurity falls into it. The ruling is that as long as no trace (color, taste, or smell) of the impurity is apparent, the water remains pure and permissible for use. The legal reasoning is that flowing water carries the impurity away, so it does not settle and become mixed. The proof includes a hadith from Abu Umamah that water is only impure if its qualities change. This is consistent with the general principle that water becomes impure only if one of its three attributes is altered. The commentary also notes the hadith of qullatayn (two qullahs) which is used by other schools to specify a quantity, but the Hanafi school does not rely on quantity alone. The author emphasizes the importance of trace effects.

Key Terms
ماء جاري (ma' jari): Flowing water that flows continuously and when taken, is replaced by other water immediately.
اوصاف ثلاثہ (awsaf thalatha): The three qualities of water: color, taste, and smell. Change in any one indicates impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does flowing water become impure if impurity falls into it?
A) As soon as impurity falls, regardless of trace.
B) Only if the impurity is visible as a solid.
C) Only if one of the water's color, taste, or smell changes.
D) Only if the water is less than two qullahs.

Key Takeaway
Flowing water is considered pure after impurity falls as long as no change in color, taste, or smell occurs; the hadith of Abu Umamah confirms this.

Ruling on a Large Pool When Impurity Falls on One Side
Ruling on large pool with impurity on one side

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using water from a large pool when impurity falls on one side, and explain the evidential basis for the position including the reliance on movement rather than quantity.

Core Idea
Movement determines purity: if impurity cannot reach, the far side remains pure.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: a large body of water where impurity falls on one side. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling based on the physical property of movement. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the Hanafi criterion for large water (ghadir 'azim) and how it differs from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the hukm for using water from the far side when impurity falls on one side? The passage states it is permissible (jā'iz) and the water remains pure (tāhir).
The ruling is for the far side; the side where impurity fell is impure.
2
Understand the definition of ghadir 'azim
What makes a pool 'large' according to the text? It is defined by lack of movement transfer: moving one side does not affect the other.
Contrast with Shafi'i definition based on quantity (two qullahs).
3
Examine the rational proof
The proof is dalil aqli: movement is stronger than impurity, so if movement does not reach, impurity cannot. Therefore the far side remains pure.
This is a rational argument, not a textual one.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa considers the lack of movement sufficient. Imam Muhammad requires a practical test to confirm movement does not reach.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.
5
Compare with Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i uses the hadith of qullatayn: water that reaches two qullahs does not carry impurity unless a quality changes.
The Hanafi response argues the hadith is weak and prefers precaution.

And the great pool (ghadir) that does not move one side by moving the other side: when impurity falls on one side, it is permissible to perform ablution from the other side, because evidently the impurity does not reach it. (40) Such a large pool that is not moving; one side moves the other side. If impurity falls on one side, ablution from the other side is permissible. Because apparently the impurity does not reach there. The pool is so long and wide that if one side of its water is moved, the effect of that movement does not reach the other side. So when the effect of movement does not reach, how will the effect of impurity reach the other side? Since the effect of movement is strong and the effect of impurity is weak. Therefore the other side remains pure, and ablution and ritual bath from it are permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa says that the consideration is from the movement; and according to Imam Muhammad, we will look by moving the water to see if it reaches the other side. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, if the water is two qullahs, it is large water; if impurity falls, as long as color, smell, or taste does not change, the water remains pure. His proof is the hadith of qullatayn that passed under issue 37. And the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa is based on precaution. (2) A basin that is ten cubits long and ten cubits wide, and deep enough that when a handful of water is taken, the ground is not seen, is also called a great pool and large water for the facility of the common people. Lexicon: al-ghadir = pool.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on a large pool (ghadir 'azim) that is so large that moving one side does not affect the other. If impurity falls on one side, the other side remains pure and can be used for ablution. The reasoning is that the impurity cannot reach the far side due to the pool's size. Imam Abu Hanifa bases the ruling on the lack of movement reaching the other side; Imam Muhammad requires a practical test. Imam al-Shafi'i uses the hadith of two qullahs to define large water and considers it pure unless a quality changes. The Hanafi school prefers the precautionary approach of relying on movement rather than quantity. The passage also defines a practical pool of ten by ten cubits deep enough for convenience.

Key Terms
غدير عظيم (ghadir 'azim): A large pool of standing water so large that moving one side does not affect the other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The water must be ten by ten cubits.
B) The impurity must not have changed any quality.
C) The movement of one side must not affect the other side.
D) The water must be two qullahs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on the physical connection of movement to determine if impurity spreads; if movement does not reach, the far side remains pure.

Ruling on Death of Animals without Flowing Blood
Ruling on animals without flowing blood in water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water purity when an animal without flowing blood dies in it and identify the proofs from Quran, Hadith, and the underlying principle.

Core Idea
Only animals with flowing blood affect water purity; the Hanafi school holds water remains pure if a fly, mosquito, etc. dies in it.

You may have heard that if a dead animal falls into water, the water becomes impure. But is that always true? This lesson examines the Hanafi position that animals without flowing blood—like flies and scorpions—do not render water impure. We will explore the textual proofs and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi ruling: water remains pure and valid for wudu when an animal without flowing blood dies in it.
The ruling is based on the impurity of flowing blood only.
2
Understand the principle (dam sa'il)
Only blood that flows from a cut (dam sa'il) is inherently impure (najis). Animals like flies lack this, so their bodies are not inherently impure.
This principle is derived from Quran and Hadith.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Quran 6:145 limits impurity to 'blood poured forth' (daman masfuhan), implying non-flowing blood is exempt.
The verse speaks about carrion and blood.
4
Examine the Hadith proof
Bukhari reports that if a fly falls into a vessel, the Prophet ordered to fully immerse it, indicating that the fly does not render the drink impure.
The command to immerse would spread impurity if the fly were impure.
5
Consider the Shafi'i ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i has two narrations: one agrees with Hanafi, another says water becomes impure. The Hanafi school follows the stronger evidence.
The Bukhari hadith supports the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وموت ماليس له دم سائل پانی کو نا پاک نہیں کرتا جیسے(۱) مچھر (۲) کھی (۳) بھڑ (۴) بچھو۔ (1) اصل میں بہتا ہوا خون ناپاک ہے اور ان جانوروں میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ان کے مرنے سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا (۲) آیت میں ہے الا ان يكون ميتة او دما مسفوحا ( آیت ۴۵ سورۃ الانعام ۶) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ بہتا ہوا خون ناپاک ہے اس لئے جس میں بہتا ہوا خون نہ ہو وہ ناپاک نہیں کرے گا (۳) حدیث سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ کھانے میں مکھی گر جائے تو کھانا نا پاک نہیں ہوتا ۔ کیونکہ اس میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہے عن ابي هريرة ان رسول الله الا الله قال اذا وقع الذباب في اناء احدكم فليغمسه كله ثم ليطرحه فان في احدى جناحيه شفاء وفي الآخر دواء (الف) ( بخاری شریف، کتاب الطب، باب از اوقع الذباب في الاناء ص۸۶۰ جلد ثانی نمبر ۵۷۸۲) حدیث میں پوری لکھی کو برتن میں ڈالنے کے لئے کہا۔ اگر مکھی سے کھانا یا پانی ناپاک ہوتا تو پوری مکھی کو کیسے ڈالنے کے لئے فرماتے (۴) دار قطنی میں ہے کہ جس جانور میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہے وہ کھانے یا پانی میں گر جائے تو اس کھانے کو کھاؤ۔ اور اس پانی سے وضو کرو قال رسول الله الله يا سلمان كل طعام و شراب وقعت فيه دابة ليس لها دم فماتت فيه فهو حلال أكله وشربه ووضوءه (ب) (دار قطنی ، باب کل طعام وقعت فيه دا به لیس لها دم ج اول ص ۳۳ نمبر (۸) دار قطنی کی حدیث اگر چہ کمزور ہے لیکن بخاری کی حدیث سے اس کی تائید ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس سے استدلال کرنا جائز ہے۔ نان امام شافعی کی ایک روایت ہمارے مطابق ہے اور ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ ان جانوروں کے مرنے سے پانی ناپاک ہو جائے گا۔
And the death of that which has no flowing blood does not make water impure, such as (1) mosquito (2) fly (3) hornet (4) scorpion. (1) In principle, flowing blood is impure, and these animals have no flowing blood. Therefore their death does not make water impure. (2) There is a verse: 'Except that it be carrion or blood poured forth' (Surah al-An'am 6:145). From this verse it is known that flowing blood is impure; therefore what has no flowing blood does not make impure. (3) Hadith indicates that if a fly falls into food, the food does not become impure, because it has no flowing blood. From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah said: 'If a fly falls into the vessel of any one of you, let him immerse it completely then throw it away, for in one wing is cure and in the other is disease.' (Bukhari) In the hadith, he ordered to immerse the entire fly. If the fly made food or water impure, why would he order to immerse the whole fly? (4) Dar Qutni reports: 'Every food and drink into which falls an animal with no blood and dies, its eating, drinking, and ablution (with water) are permissible.' Although the hadith of Dar Qutni is weak, it is supported by Bukhari's hadith, so deducing from it is permissible. And Imam al-Shafi'i has one narration that matches our view and another that these animals' death does make water impure.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that the death of animals without flowing blood (like flies, mosquitoes, etc.) does not render water impure. The proof includes: (1) the inherent impurity is flowing blood, which these animals lack; (2) Quranic verse limiting impurity to 'blood poured forth'; (3) hadith of the fly showing that immersion is commanded, indicating no impurity; (4) a hadith from Dar Qutni explicitly allowing use of water in which such an animal died. Although the Dar Qutni hadith is weak, it is supported by the stronger Bukhari hadith. The passage notes that Imam al-Shafi'i has two narrations: one agreeing with the Hanafi position and one saying the water becomes impure. The Hanafi school relies on the majority of evidence.

Key Terms
دم سائل (dam sa'il): Flowing blood; blood that flows when the animal's vein is cut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The water is impure because scorpions are poisonous.
B) The water remains pure because scorpions have no flowing blood.
C) The water becomes impure because scorpions have blood.
D) The ruling is unknown.

Key Takeaway
Death of an animal without flowing blood does not render water impure according to the Hanafi school.

Ruling on Still Water That Does Not Transmit Impurity
Hanafi ruling on pond water with intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on impurity in still water and distinguish between the criteria of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding transmission.

Core Idea
Still water with no flow: impurity on one side does not transmit unless movement from source reaches the other side.

This passage addresses a practical question: if najasah (impurity) falls on one side of a still pond, is the other side still pure for wudu? The author presents the general ruling, then dives into an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad about what constitutes 'movement' that can carry impurity. Finally, the Hanafi definition of a large pond (ma' kathir) is given for convenience. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the condition of water flow and the different criteria used by the Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and overall ruling
The passage deals with a still pond where water does not flow from one side to the other. The ruling: wudu from the clean side is valid because impurity apparently does not reach it.
The key condition is the absence of movement (flow).
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa considers 'movement from the source' (natural flow) as the criterion for impurity transmission. Imam Muhammad considers movement caused by the act of wudu (user-induced) – if taking water causes ripples to reach the impure side, the clean side becomes impure.
Both views are within the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi is not specified here.
3
Compare with Imam al-Shafi'i's view
Imam al-Shafi'i uses the hadith of qullatain: water of 2 qullahs (≈190 litres) is only impure if color, taste, or smell changes. The Hanafi school takes a more precautionary approach (ihtiyat) based on physical movement.
This is a cross-madhhab difference with practical implications.
4
Apply the Hanafi definition of ma' kathir
The passage defines a large pond (ghadir) as 10 cubits long × 10 cubits wide, with depth such that the bottom is not visible when water is scooped. This is considered ma' kathir for convenience.
This definition is practical for determining when water is abundant; the earlier dispute on movement still applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الذي لا يتحرك احد طرفيه بتحريك الطرف الآخر اذا وقعت في احد جانبيه نجاسة جاز الوضوء من الجانب الآخر لان الظاهر ان النجاسة لاتصل اليه امام ابوحنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نسل سے حرکت دینے کا اعتبار ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک وضو سے حرکت دیکر دیکھیں گے کہ دوسری جانب پہنچتا ہے یا نہیں۔ ن امام شافعی کے نزدیک دو مکے پانی ہو تو وہ ماء کثیر ہے۔ اس میں نجاست گر جائے تو جب تک رنگ، بو یا مزا نہ بدل جائے تو پانی پاک رہے گا۔ ان کی دلیل حدیث قکتین [قکتین؟] ہے جو مسئلہ نمبر ۳۷ میں گزرگئی۔ وت امام ابو حنیفہ کا مسلک احتیاط پر مبنی ہے (۲) دس ہاتھ لمبا اور دس ہاتھ چوڑا حوض ہو اور اتنا گہرا ہو کہ پانی کا چلواٹھانے سے زمین نظر نہ آئے تو اس کو بھی عوام کی سہولت کے لئے بڑا تالاب اور ماء کثیر کہتے ہیں ۔ لغت الغدير : تالاب
That which one side does not move by moving the other side, when najasah falls on one side, wudu is permissible from the other side because apparently the najasah does not reach it. Imam Abu Hanifa says: consideration is movement from the source. According to Imam Muhammad, we look at movement from wudu to see if it reaches the other side. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, if there are two qullas of water, it is ma' kathir. If najasah falls into it, the water remains pure as long as color, smell, or taste does not change. His proof is the hadith of qullatain, which passed in issue no. 37. The madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa is based on precaution. (2) A pool ten cubits long and ten cubits wide and so deep that the bottom is not visible when water is scooped, this is also called a large pond and ma' kathir for the convenience of the people. Lexicon: al-ghadir: pond.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling about a still pond: if the water does not flow from one side to the other (i.e., no current), then impurity falling on one side does not affect the other side, and wudu from the other side is valid. The author then discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa considers the movement of the water itself (if it flows from one side to the other) as the criterion for impurity transmission, while Imam Muhammad considers whether the act of wudu causes water movement to reach the impure side. Imam al-Shafi'i's view is also mentioned: if the water reaches two qullahs (about 190 litres), it is considered flowing and impurity only affects it if color, taste, or smell changes; otherwise it remains pure. The Hanafi school, however, takes a more precautionary approach. Finally, the passage defines a large pond (ghadir) of 10x10 cubits with sufficient depth as 'ma' kathir' for practical convenience.

Key Terms
ماء كثير (ma' kathir): Water that is abundant; here defined as a pond 10x10 cubits with depth such that bottom is not visible when scooped.
غدير (ghadir): A pond or pool of water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Still water remains pure on the opposite side unless natural or wudu-induced movement carries the impurity.

Death of Animals Without Flowing Blood Does Not Impurify Water
Ruling with proofs: animals without flowing blood do not spoil water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water containing dead insects without flowing blood, and prove it using the Quranic verse 'dam masfuh' and the hadith of the fly.

Core Idea
Animals without flowing blood do not impurify water because only flowing blood (dam masfuh) is najis by Quranic text.

This lesson examines a specific purity ruling: when a small insect dies in water, does the water become impure? The Hanafi school says no, based on the principle that najasah requires flowing blood. We will trace the proofs from Quran and Sunnah and see how the school distinguishes between different types of dead animals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The death of an animal that lacks flowing blood (like a mosquito or fly) in water. The ruling: the water remains pure (tahir).
The key factor is the presence or absence of flowing blood (nafs sa'ilah).
2
Locate the primary dalil (Quran)
The author cites Surah al-An'am 6:145: 'except that it be dead or poured forth blood' (illa an yakuna maytatan aw daman masfuhan). This verse indicates that only flowing blood is impure.
The term 'masfuh' (poured forth) implies blood that flows, not stagnant blood.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the verse prove the ruling? Since these animals have no flowing blood, they are not included in the category of impure things. Their dead bodies do not transfer najasah.
Hanafi usul: al-mantuq (what is mentioned) implies the opposite in this case.
4
Support with hadith evidence
The hadith of the fly (Bukhari) orders immersing the fly completely if it falls into a vessel. If the fly made the water impure, this would not be ordered. A second hadith (al-Daraqutni) explicitly states that food/drink with a dead bloodless animal is permissible.
The Daraqutni hadith is weak but supported by the stronger Bukhari hadith.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
Imam al-Shafi'i has two narrations: one agrees with the Hanafi position, the other considers the water impure (because the dead animal is a maytah). The Hanafi position is mufta bihi based on the clear Quranic text.
The difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is preferred due to stronger textual evidence.

(۴۰) پانی میں ایسی چیز کا مرنا جس میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہے پانی کو نا پاک نہیں کرتا جیسے (۱) مچھر (۲) کھی [مکھی] (۳) بھڑ (۴) بچھو۔ (۱) اصل میں بہتا ہوا خون ناپاک ہے اور ان جانوروں میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ان کے مرنے سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا (۲) آیت میں ہے الا ان يكون ميتة او دما مسفوحا ( آیت ۴۵ سورۃ الانعام ۶) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ بہتا ہوا خون ناپاک ہے اس لئے جس میں بہتا ہوا خون نہ ہو وہ ناپاک نہیں کرے گا (۳) حدیث سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ کھانے میں مکھی گر جائے تو کھانا نا پاک نہیں ہوتا ۔ کیونکہ اس میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہے عن ابي هريرة ان رسول الله الا الله قال اذا وقع الذباب في اناء احدكم فليغمسه كله ثم ليطرحه فان في احدى جناحيه شفاء وفي الآخر دواء (الف) ( بخاری شریف، کتاب الطب، باب از اوقع الذباب في الاناء ص۸۶۰ جلد ثانی نمبر ۵۷۸۲) حدیث میں پوری لکھی [مکھی] کو برتن میں ڈالنے کے لئے کہا۔ اگر مکھی سے کھانا یا پانی ناپاک ہوتا تو پوری مکھی کو کیسے ڈالنے کے لئے فرماتے (۴) دار قطنی میں ہے کہ جس جانور میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہے وہ کھانے یا پانی میں گر جائے تو اس کھانے کو کھاؤ۔ اور اس پانی سے وضو کرو قال رسول الله الله یا سلمان كل طعام و شراب وقعت فيه دابة ليس لها دم فماتت فيه فهو حلال أكله و شربه و وضوءه (ب) (دار قطنی ، باب کل طعام وقعت فيه دا به لیس لها دم ج اول ص ۳۳ نمبر (۸) دار قطنی کی حدیث اگر چہ کمزور ہے لیکن بخاری کی حدیث سے اس کی تائید ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس سے استدلال کرنا جائز ہے۔ نان امام شافعی کی ایک روایت ہمارے مطابق ہے اور ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ ان جانوروں کے مرنے سے پانی ناپاک ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا اگر کبھی تم میں سے کسی کے برتن میں گر جائے تو پورے ہی کو ڈ بود و پھر اس کو نکال کر پھینک دو۔ اس لئے کہ اس کے ایک پر میں شفا ہے اور دوسرے میں بیماری ہے ( ب ) آپ نے فرمایا، اے سلمان ! ہر وہ کھانا اور پینا جس میں ایسا جانور گر جائے جس میں خون نہیں ہوتا اور اس میں مرجائے تو اس کا کھانا اور اس کا پینا اور اس سے وضو کر نا حلال ہے۔
(40) The death of something that does not have flowing blood in water does not make the water impure, such as (1) mosquito, (2) fly, (3) hornet, (4) scorpion. (1) Basically, flowing blood is impure, and these animals do not have flowing blood. Therefore, their death does not make water impure. (2) In the verse: 'except that it be dead or poured forth blood' (Surah al-An'am 6:145). From this verse it is known that flowing blood is impure; thus whatever does not have flowing blood will not make impure. (3) The hadith indicates that if a fly falls into food, the food does not become impure, because it does not have flowing blood. From Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'If a fly falls into the vessel of one of you, let him immerse it completely, then throw it away, for in one wing is cure and in the other is disease.' (Bukhari, Kitab al-Tibb, Bab Idha Waqa'a al-Dhubab fi al-Ina', vol. 2, p. 860, no. 5782). In the hadith, he ordered to immerse the whole fly. If the fly made the food or water impure, how could he order to immerse the whole fly? (4) In al-Daraqutni: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'O Salman, every food and drink into which falls an animal that has no blood and dies therein, its eating, drinking, and performing wudu with it are permissible.' (al-Daraqutni, Bab Kullu Ta'am Waqa'at Fihi Dabbatun Laysa Laha Dam, vol. 1, p. 33, no. 8). Although the hadith of al-Daraqutni is weak, it is supported by the hadith of Bukhari, so deducing from it is permissible. As for Imam al-Shafi'i, one of his narrations is in agreement with us, and another is that the death of these animals makes the water impure. Therefore, (commentary: He said: 'If ever a fly falls into the vessel of one of you, immerse it completely then throw it away, for in one wing is cure and in the other is disease.' He said: 'O Salman, every food and drink into which falls an animal that has no blood and dies therein, its eating, drinking, and performing wudu with it are permissible.')
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs. It states that animals without flowing blood (such as mosquitoes, flies, hornets, scorpions) do not render water impure when they die in it. The reason is that flowing blood (dam masfuh) is impure by Quranic text (Surah al-An'am 6:145), and these creatures lack it. The author supports this with two hadith: (1) The famous hadith of the fly: if a fly falls into a vessel, one is instructed to immerse it entirely, which implies the water remains pure. (2) A hadith from al-Daraqutni stating that any insect without blood that falls into food/drink and dies makes it permissible. Although the latter is weak, it is strengthened by the Bukhari hadith. Finally, the author notes a difference with Imam al-Shafi'i: one of his narrations agrees, another considers such water impure because the dead animal is a carcass (maytah) and carcasses are impure.

Key Terms
نفس سائلة (nafs sa'ilah): Flowing blood that is considered najis.
ميتة (maytah): A dead animal that has not been slaughtered Islamically.
دم مسفوح (dam masfuh): Poured forth blood; flowing blood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence the author uses to prove that animals without flowing blood do not impurify water?
A) The hadith about immersing a fly in a vessel.
B) The Quranic verse about flowing blood being impure.
C) Consensus of the Sahaba.
D) Analogy with aquatic animals.

Key Takeaway
Only animals with flowing blood (nafs sa'ilah) impurify water when they die in it; those without it leave the water pure.

The Death of Aquatic Animals Does Not Impurify Water
Ruling with proof: aquatic animals like fish, frog, crab do not spoil water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on aquatic animal death in water and explain the proof from hadith and the illah of flowing blood.

Core Idea
Aquatic animals lack flowing blood, so their death does not make water impure.

When an animal dies in water, does it become impure? The Hanafi school answers based on a key factor: whether the animal has flowing blood. Aquatic creatures like fish, frogs, and crabs do not possess true flowing blood, as evidenced by their blood turning white in sunlight. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof from hadith, also addressing an inter-madhhab difference with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the death of an aquatic animal (e.g., fish, frog, crab) in water. The Hanafi ruling: water remains pure (tahir) and can be used for purification.
This applies to any water, whether little or large, according to the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the hadith: 'Its water is purifying and its dead is permissible.' (Tirmidhi) This indicates that the dead body of sea creatures is not impure.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain), thus zanni al-thubut, but its dalala is qat'i regarding the purity of the dead.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'al-hillu maytatuhu' (its dead is permissible) implies that the dead is halal in the sense of being pure (tahir), not necessarily edible. The Hanafi understanding: 'halal' here means not impure, because impurity would prevent usage. Further, the text argues that aquatic animals lack flowing blood, which is the effective cause for impurity from dead animals.
The absence of flowing blood is supported by the observation that their blood turns white in sunlight, unlike true blood.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i (in one narration) holds that only fish (halal to eat) do not spoil water; other aquatic animals (like frog, crab) spoil a small amount of water. Their basis: the hadith's permissibility is linked to edibility.
The Hanafi response: the hadith is general for all sea creatures, and the illah is absence of flowing blood, not halal status.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and considered stronger because it relies on a clear illah (absence of flowing blood) and the general application of the hadith. The Shafi'i restriction to edible animals is extra conditions not present in the text.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is consistent with the principle that animals without flowing blood do not make water impure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۱) وموت ما يعيش في الماء لايفسد الـمـاء كالسمك والضفدع والسرطان (۱) جو جانور پانی میں پیدا ہوتا ہے اور اسی میں زندگی گزارتا ہے اس میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ بہتا ہوا خون رہے گا تو پانی کے اندر ہی نہیں رسکے گا۔ اور وہ جو تھوڑا بہت خون نظر آتا ہے وہ مکمل خون نہیں ہے۔ خون کی خاصیت یہ ہے کہ اس کو دھوپ میں رکھو تو وہ کالا سا ہو جائے گا۔ اور دریائی جانور کے خون کو دھوپ میں رکھو تو وہ سفید ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ مکمل خون ہی نہیں ہے۔ اور مسئلہ نمبر ۴۰ میں تفصیل سے گزر چکا ہے کہ جس جانور میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہے اس کے مرنے سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم هو الطهور ماء ه الحل ميتته (الف) ( ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی ماء البحرانه ظهور ص ۲۱ نمبر ۶۹) سمندر کا میتہ حلال ہے سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ کھانا تو حلال نہیں ہے لیکن اس کے مردے میں خون نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس کے مرنے سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ فا امام شافعی کی ایک روایت ہے کہ مچھلی کے علاوہ دوسرے مائی جانور کے مرنے سے تھوڑا پانی ناپاک ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ مچھلی تو حلال ہے لیکن دوسرے جانور حلال نہیں ہیں اس لئے دوسرے جانور کے مرنے سے تھوڑا پانی ناپاک ہوگا۔
(41) The death of what lives in water does not spoil the water, such as fish, frog, crab. (1) The animal that is created in water and lives in it does not have flowing blood. Because if it had flowing blood, it would not flow inside water. And the little blood that is seen is not complete blood. The property of blood is that if you keep it in the sun, it becomes black. But the blood of sea animals becomes white in the sun. Therefore, it is not complete blood. And it has passed in detail in issue no. 40 that an animal without flowing blood does not make water impure by its death. (2) From Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Its water is purifying and its dead is permissible.' (Tirmidhi, Kitab ma Ja'a fi Ma' al-Bahr annahu Tahur, p. 21, no. 69). From 'its dead is permissible' it can be inferred that the dead of the sea is halal. It does not have blood, so its death does not make water impure. As for Imam al-Shafi'i, one narration is that besides fish, death of other aquatic animals makes a small amount of water impure, because fish is halal but other aquatic animals are not halal; thus their death impurifies small water.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This ruling states that aquatic animals (fish, frog, crab) do not spoil water when they die in it. The reason is that they do not possess flowing blood; their blood is not true blood, as evidenced by it turning white in sunlight. The author also refers to the hadith about sea water being pure and its dead being permissible, indicating that fish do not have impure blood. A difference with Imam al-Shafi'i is noted: he considers only fish (halal) as not spoiling water, while other aquatic animals may spoil a small amount because they are not halal to eat. The Hanafi view is that all aquatic animals without flowing blood are like other non-flowing-blood creatures.

Key Terms
مائي جانور (ma'i janwar): Aquatic animal that lives in water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis consider the death of a frog in water not to spoil the water?
A) Because frogs are not mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because frogs do not have flowing blood; their blood turns white in sunlight.
C) Because frogs are halal to eat.
D) Because frogs are small animals.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the death of any aquatic animal (fish, frog, crab, etc.) does not make water impure because they lack flowing blood.

The Ruling on Used Water: Pure but Not Purifying
Ruling on used water: pure but not purifying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ma' musta'mal and distinguish between its purity (taharah) and its lack of purificatory property (tahur).

Core Idea
Water used for worship is pure but loses the power to purify.

After learning the categories of pure water, we now examine water that has been used in acts of worship—wudu, ghusl, or other qurbah. According to the Hanafi school, such water remains intrinsically pure, but it cannot be used again to remove ritual impurity. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Recognize that the topic is water which has been used in an act of worship (wudu, ghusl, or any qurbah). This is called ma' musta'mal.
It is not the water that becomes impure by contact with najasah.
2
Determine the dual ruling
The Hanafi position: ma' musta'mal is tahir (pure) but not mutahhir (purifying). It is pure in itself but cannot remove hadath. Accept this as the school's settled view.
This distinguishes it from both pure water (tahur) and impure water (najis).
3
Examine the first proof
Two practical arguments: (1) The Companions' clothes had used water from wudu/ghusl, yet they never washed them for that reason—so it is not impure. (2) The Arabs, despite severe water scarcity, never reused such water for wudu or stored it for that purpose—implying it lacks purificatory ability.
These are inductive proofs from the practice of the early community.
4
Examine the second proof
The hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave water he used for wudu to sick people to drink. This shows the water is pure enough to consume, otherwise he would not have offered it.
This reinforces the purity aspect, not the purificatory aspect.
5
Apply the ruling practically
When performing wudu or ghusl, the water that runs off the body is ma' musta'mal. It should not be collected and reused for purification, but it is not najis.
You may still use it for other purposes like drinking or cleaning (provided no hadath is involved).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۲) اور ماء مستعمل نہیں جائز ہے اس کا استعمال کرنا حدث کے پاک کرنے میں۔ تشر جس پانی کو حدث غسل یا حدث وضو کو زائل کرنے کے لئے استعمال کیا ہو یا قربت حاصل کرنے کے لئے استعمال کیا ہوا ایسے پانی کو دو بارہ حدث غسل یا حدث وضو کو پاک کرنے کے لئے استعمال کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ پانی مستعمل ہو چکا ہے۔ اور ماء مستعمل خود پاک تو ہے لیکن حدث کو پاک کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا۔ (۱) پاک ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ماء مستعمل صحابہ کے کپڑوں میں وضو اور غسل کے بعد لگتا رہا لیکن آج تک کسی نے ماء مستعمل کی وجہ سے کپڑا انہیں دھویا۔ اور پاک کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اہل عرب کو پانی کی سخت ضرورت ہونے کے باوجود کسی نے ماء مستعمل استعمال کر کے وضو یا غسل نہیں کیا۔ اور نہ اس کو دوسرے برتن میں وضو یا غسل کے لئے رکھا ہو (۲) پاک ہونے کی دلیل وہ احادیث ہیں جن میں حضور نے وضو کے لئے استعمال کیا ہوا پانی مریضوں کو پلایا ہے۔ اگر ماء مستعمل پاک نہ ہوتا تو آپ اس کو بیمارون کو کیسے حاشیہ : (الف) سمندر کا پانی پاک ہے اور اس کا مردہ ( یعنی مچھلی ) حلال ہے۔
(42) And used water (ma' musta'mal): it is not permissible to use it for removing hadath. Explanation: Water that has been used to remove hadath of ghusl or hadath of wudu, or used to gain closeness (qurbah), such water cannot be used again to purify hadath ghusl or hadath wudu. Because this water has been used. And used water is pure in itself, but it does not have the capability to purify hadath. (1) The evidence for it being pure is that used water remained on the clothes of the Companions after wudu and ghusl, but no one ever washed their clothes because of used water. And the evidence that it does not have purifying capability is that even though the Arabs had severe need for water, no one performed wudu or ghusl with used water, nor did they store it in another vessel for wudu or ghusl. (2) The evidence for its purity is the hadith in which the Prophet gave water he used for wudu to sick people to drink. If used water were not pure, how could he give it to the sick? (Footnote: The water of the sea is pure and its dead (i.e., fish) is permissible.)
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on used water (ma' musta'mal). The Hanafi position is that water which has been used to remove ritual impurity (hadath) or to perform an act of worship (qurbah) is considered 'used'. Such water is intrinsically pure (tahir), but it loses its ability to purify (tahur). The author provides two proofs: (1) The Companions' clothes had used water on them, yet they did not wash them for that reason, indicating it is not impure. (2) The Prophet (peace be upon him) gave used wudu water to the sick, showing it is pure. The lack of purifying capability is proven by the fact that even in water scarcity, Arabs never reused it for wudu or ghusl, implying it does not have that property. Note: a footnote repeats the sea water ruling from earlier.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used in wudu, ghusl, or other acts of worship; it is pure but not purifying.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that requires wudu (minor) or ghusl (major) to be removed.
قربت (qurbah): An act of worship seeking closeness to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this text, why is used water (ma' musta'mal) considered not purifying?
A) Because it becomes najis after use.
B) Because it loses its chemical properties.
C) Because the Arabs refrained from using it for wudu despite water scarcity.
D) Because it becomes warm after use.

Key Takeaway
Ma' musta'mal is pure but not purifying: it can be drunk but not used to remove hadath.

Ruling on Aquatic Creatures Dying in Water
Ruling with proof: death of aquatic creatures and water purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the purity of water when an aquatic animal dies in it and explain the proof from hadith and the rational argument about flowing blood.

Core Idea
An aquatic animal's death does not spoil water because it lacks flowing blood – impurity depends on blood, not edibility.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from the chapter of Taharah: what happens when an animal that lives in water dies in it? The Hanafi school holds that such an event does not make the water impure, based on a clear prophetic hadith and a rational analysis of blood characteristics. We will also encounter a legitimate inter-madhhab disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i, which will sharpen your understanding of how proofs are weighed in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
First, note that the passage states the death of 'what lives in water' (fish, frog, crab) does not spoil water. Also, creatures with flowing blood that die in water (like flies, wasps) also do not spoil water because they lack flowing blood – a reference to a previous rule.
The key distinction is the presence or absence of flowing blood (nafs sa'ila).
2
Locate the primary proof – the hadith
The author cites the hadith about sea water: 'It is pure, its water is purifying, and its dead is lawful.' This hadith directly indicates that the dead of the sea (which includes fish and other aquatic creatures) is not impure, as impurity would prevent lawfulness.
The hadith is reported in Sunan al-Tirmidhi; its chains are ahad, but the Hanafi school accepts it as sufficient for this ruling.
3
Examine the rational proof – condition of blood
The passage provides a rational proof: aquatic animals do not have true flowing blood because their blood does not turn black in the sun like the blood of land animals. Thus, they fall under the earlier rule that animals without flowing blood do not spoil water when they die in it.
This is an example of istihsan or supplemental reasoning, confirming the hadith's implication.
4
Identify the inter-madhhab dispute
The author mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i (in one narration) holds that aquatic animals other than fish make a small amount of water impure. His proof: only fish is lawful to eat, so the dead of other aquatic animals are impure.
The Hanafi response is that edibility and impurity are separate issues; the key criterion is flowing blood, not lawfulness of consumption.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In the Hanafi school, water remains pure when any aquatic animal dies in it. In the Shafi'i view, the water becomes impure if the animal is not fish and the water is a small amount (less than two qullas). This difference affects daily practice, e.g., using water from a well where a crab has died.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the position of purity, based on the hadith and the rational proof.

Source Text

نفس سائلة في الماء لا يفسد الماء كالبق والذباب والزنابير والعقارب (41) وموت ما يعيش في الماء لايفسد الـمـاء كالسمك والضفدع والسرطان (42) واما الماء
کہ یہ جانور میتہ ہے اور ان کا کھانا حرام ہے۔ اور میتہ ناپاک ہوتا ہے اس لئے ان کے مرنے سے پانی ناپاک ہو جائے گا۔ نفس سائلہ : بہتا ہوا خون البق : مچھر - الذباب بکھی۔ الزنا بیر : بھڑ - العقارب : بچھو، عقرب کی جمع ہے۔
(41) مرنا ایسی چیز کا جو پانی میں زندگی گزارتی ہو پانی کو نا پاک نہیں کرتی ہے جیسے (1) مچھلی (2) مینڈک (3) کیکڑا ۔ (1) جو جانور پانی میں پیدا ہوتا ہے اور اسی میں زندگی گزارتا ہے اس میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ بہتا ہوا خون رہے گا تو پانی کے اندر ہی نہیں رسکے گا۔ اور وہ جو تھوڑا بہت خون نظر آتا ہے وہ مکمل خون نہیں ہے۔ خون کی خاصیت یہ ہے کہ اس کو دھوپ میں رکھو تو وہ کالا سا ہو جائے گا۔ اور دریائی جانور کے خون کو دھوپ میں رکھو تو وہ سفید ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ مکمل خون ہی نہیں ہے۔ اور مسئلہ نمبر 40 میں تفصیل سے گزر چکا ہے کہ جس جانور میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہے اس کے مرنے سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ (2) عن ابي هريرة قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم هو الطهور ماء ه الحل ميتته (الف) ( ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی ماء البحرانه ظهور ص 21 نمبر 69) سمندر کا میتہ حلال ہے سے استدلال کیا جا
سکتا ہے کہ کھانا تو حلال نہیں ہے لیکن اس کے مردے میں خون نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس کے مرنے سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ فا امام شافعی کی ایک روایت ہے کہ مچھلی کے علاوہ دوسرے مائی جانور کے مرنے سے تھوڑا پانی ناپاک ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ مچھلی تو حلال ہے لیکن دوسرے جانور حلال نہیں ہیں اس لئے دوسرے جانور کے مرنے سے تھوڑا پانی ناپاک ہوگا۔
الضفدع : مینڈک۔ السرطان : کیکڑا۔ جو جانور پانی میں پیدا ہوتا ہے اور پانی ہی میں زندگی گزارتا ہے وہ مائی جانور کہلاتا ہے۔ اور جو پانی کے اوپر پیدا ہوتا ہے اور پانی میں رہتا ہے وہ مائی جانور نہیں ہے جیسے بلخ۔
Flowing blood in water does not spoil water, like mosquitoes, flies, wasps, and scorpions (41). And the death of what lives in water does not spoil water, like fish, frog, and crab (42). As for water: [Urdu: Because these animals are dead and their eating is forbidden. And a dead thing is impure, so their death would make the water impure. Flowing blood: flowing blood. Al-baqq: mosquitoes. Al-dhubab: flies. Al-zanabir: wasps. Al-aqarib: scorpions, plural of aqrab.] (41) The death of something that lives in water does not make water impure, like (1) fish, (2) frog, (3) crab. (1) An animal that is born in water and lives in it does not have flowing blood. Because if it had flowing blood, it would not flow inside water. And the little blood that appears is not complete blood. The property of blood is that if you put it in the sun, it becomes blackish. But the blood of a sea animal becomes white when put in sun. So it is not complete blood. And issue no. 40 has already passed in detail that the death of an animal without flowing blood does not make water impure. (2) From Abu Hurayrah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'It is pure, its water is purifying, its dead is lawful' (a) (Tirmidhi, chapter on what has come about sea water being purifying, p. 21, no. 69). It can be deduced that the dead of the sea is lawful, but it is not lawful to eat, yet its dead does not have blood, so its death does not make water impure. Imam al-Shafi'i has a narration that the death of other aquatic animals besides fish makes a small amount of water impure, because fish is lawful but other animals are not, so their death makes small water impure. Al-dafda': frog. Al-sartan: crab. An animal that is born in water and lives in water is called an aquatic animal. And one that is born above water but lives in water is not aquatic, like the duck.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter of Taharah. It states that the death of animals with flowing blood (like flies, wasps) in water does not spoil it, because they lack the flowing blood that would make the water impure. Similarly, animals that live entirely in water (fish, frog, crab) do not spoil water upon death because they either have no flowing blood or their blood is not considered true blood. The author provides a rational proof: aquatic animals have blood that does not behave like typical blood (it turns white in sun). He then cites the hadith about sea water being purifying and its dead being lawful, which indicates that sea animals' dead bodies are not impure. The passage also notes a disagreement: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that other aquatic animals besides fish make a small amount of water impure, because only fish is lawful to eat. However, the Hanafi position, based on the hadith and reasoning about blood, is that all creatures without flowing blood do not spoil water.

Key Terms
نفس سائلة (nafs sa'ila): Flowing blood that comes out when a vein is cut, as opposed to blood that does not flow.
مائي جانور (ma'i janwar): An animal that is born and lives entirely in water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to water when a crab dies in it?
A) The water becomes impure because crabs are not eaten.
B) The water remains pure because crabs have no flowing blood.
C) The water becomes impure only if it is a small amount.
D) The water becomes pure but not purifying.

Key Takeaway
The death of an aquatic animal or any creature without flowing blood does not make water impure in the Hanafi school, based on the hadith and the illa of flowing blood.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Used Water (Mā' Musta'mal)
Establishes that used water is pure but not purifying for hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on used water (mā' musta'mal) and explain the evidence from the Sunnah that supports it.

Core Idea
Used water is pure but not purifying—it can quench thirst but not remove ritual impurity.

In this lesson, we examine the legal status of water that has already been used to remove ritual impurity. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the water's inherent purity (tahārah) and its capacity to purify (tahūriyyah). You will learn the definition, the ruling, and the textual proofs from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Define mā' musta'mal
Identify what counts as used water: water used to remove hadath (ritual impurity) or used on the body as an act of devotion.
Water used to remove actual impurity (najāsat 'ayniyya) becomes impure, not just 'used'.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
State that the water is pure (tāhir) but not purifying (tahūr). It is permissible to drink or use for non-ritual purposes, but not for wudu or ghusl.
This is the muftā bihī position.
3
Identify proofs for purity
List the hadith where the Prophet gave his wudu water to the sick to drink, and the practice of the Companions not washing clothes wet with used water.
These show the water is not impure.
4
Identify proofs for non-purifying
Cite the hadith where the Prophet took fresh water for each limb during wudu, and the prohibition of bathing in standing water while junub.
These show the water lacks purifying capacity.
5
Note ikhtilaf and tarjih
Acknowledge that some early Hanafis held it impure, and the Shafi'i school holds it purifying if unchanged. The Hanafi tarjih (preponderance) is that it is pure but not purifying, based on the hadith evidence.
The author of al-Hidayah asserts this as the correct view.

المستعمل لا يجوز استعماله في طهارة الاحداث (43) والماء المستعمل كل ماء ازيل به حدث غسل او وضوء او استعمل في البدن على وجه القربة
تشر جس پانی کو حدث غسل یا حدث وضو کو زائل کرنے کے لئے استعمال کیا ہو یا قربت حاصل کرنے کے لئے استعمال کیا ہوا ایسے پانی کو دو بارہ حدث غسل یا حدث وضو کو پاک کرنے کے لئے استعمال کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ پانی مستعمل ہو چکا ہے۔ اور ماء مستعمل خود پاک تو ہے لیکن حدث کو پاک کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا۔
(1) پاک ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ماء مستعمل صحابہ کے کپڑوں میں وضو اور غسل کے بعد لگتا رہا لیکن آج تک کسی نے ماء مستعمل کی وجہ سے کپڑا انہیں دھویا۔ اور پاک کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اہل کے لئے استعمال کیا ہوا پانی مریضوں کو پلایا ہے۔ اگر ماء مستعمل پاک نہ ہوتا تو آپ اس کو بیمارون کیسے پلاتے؟ حدیث میں ہے عن جابر يقول جاء رسول الله لا يعودني وانا مريض لا اعقل فتوضأ وصب على من وضوئه فعقلت (الف) بخاری شریف، باب حب النبی و وضوء علی المی علی ص 32 نمبر193)(3)سمعت السائب بن يزيد يقول ذهبت بـي خـالـتـي الـى النبي فقالت يا رسول الله ان ابن اختي وقع فمسح رأسى ودعا لي بالبركة ثم توضأ فشربت من وضوء ه (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب استعمال فضل وضوء الناس ص 31 نمبر 19) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ماء مستعمل پاک ہے تب ہی تو وضوء 31 سے معلوم ہوا ماری وضو کا پانی پلایا۔ اور السنن الکبری سبیھقی ، باب غرفة بيده اليمنى فتمضمض واستنشق ثم اخذ اخرى فجمع بها يديه ثم غسل وجهه الخ (ج ) ( ابوداؤد، باب فی الوضوء مرتین ص 20 نمبر 137) اس حدیث میں ہر عضو کے لئے الگ الگ پانی لیا گیا ہے۔ ایک اور حدیث میں تھوڑے پانی میں جنابت کے غسل کرنے سے منع فرمایا ۔ اگر اس کے جسم پر نجاست نہ ہو تو منع کرنے کی یہی وجہ ہو سکتی ہے کہ ماء مستعمل ہونے کے بعد وہ پانی دوسروں کے کام نہیں آسکتا۔ اس لئے اس میں گھس کر پانی کومستعمل کرنے سے منع فرمایا۔ حدیث میں ہے ابو هريرة يقول قال رسول الله الا الله لا يغتسل احدكم في الماء الدائم وهو جنب (و) (مسلم شریف ، باب النھی عن الاغتسال في الماء الرا کد ص 138 نمبر 283) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ماء مستعمل پاک تو ہے لیکن پاک کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے ما مستعمل کے حکم کے سلسے میں کئی قول نقل کئے ہیں۔ لیکن اثر ائمہ کا صح قول یہی ہے کہ وہ پاک ہے لیکن پاک کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا۔ کما قال موسوعۃ الامام الشافعی ، باب حكم الماء مستعمل ج اول ص 52) (43) ماء مستعمل ہر وہ پانی ہے جس سے حدث زائل کیا گیا ہو (2) یا بدن پر قربت کے طور پر استعمال کیا گیا ہو۔ (1) اگر عینی نجاست بدن یا کپڑے پر ہو اس کو پانی سے دور کیا تو وہ پانی ناپاک ہے۔ البتہ نجاست عینی نہ ہو صرف حدث اکبر جنابت یا حدث اصغر وضو کرنے کے لئے پانی استعمال کیا تو وہ ماء مستعمل ہوتا ہے (2) یا پہلے وضو موجود ہو لیکن قربت الہی حاصل کرنے کے لئے دوبارہ وضو کرے تو یہ بھی ماء مستعمل ہو جاتا ہے۔ جس کا حکم اوپر گذر چکا۔
Used water: It is not permissible to use it for the purification of hadath (43). And used water is every water with which hadath of ghusl or wudu has been removed, or which has been used on the body as an act of devotion. [Urdu: The water that has been used to remove hadath of ghusl or hadath of wudu, or used to gain closeness (to Allah), such water is not permissible to use again to purify hadath of ghusl or wudu, because it has become used. And used water is itself pure but does not have the capacity to purify hadath. (1) The proof that it is pure is that used water would cling to the clothes of the Companions after wudu and ghusl, but no one ever washed their clothes because of used water. And the proof that it does not have purifying capacity is that despite the severe need for water among the Arabs, no one performed wudu or ghusl with used water, nor did they store it for that purpose. (2) Another proof of its purity is the hadiths in which the Prophet gave used water to the sick to drink. If used water were impure, how would he give it to the sick? There is a hadith from Jabir: 'The Messenger of Allah came to visit me while I was sick and unconscious. He performed wudu and poured the water of his wudu on me, and I became conscious.' (a) (Bukhari, chapter on the Prophet's love and wudu on the sick, p. 32 no. 193). (3) I heard al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid say: 'My aunt took me to the Prophet and said, O Messenger of Allah, my nephew is afflicted. So he wiped my head and prayed for blessing for me, then performed wudu, and I drank from the water of his wudu.' (b) (Bukhari, chapter on using leftover water of people's wudu, p. 31 no. 19). From these hadiths it is known that used water is pure; otherwise, how could they drink it? And in al-Sunan al-Kubra by al-Bayhaqi (chapter on the purity of used water, vol. 1 p. 359 no. 117) many hadiths on this topic are mentioned. As for used water not being purifying, deduction is made from the hadiths in which the Prophet took fresh water for each limb. If used water were purifying, he would have reused it and not taken fresh water for each limb. A hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'Do you want me to show you how the Messenger of Allah performed wudu? He called for a vessel with water, took a handful with his right hand, rinsed his mouth and nose, then took another, combined his hands, and washed his face...' (c) (Abu Dawud, chapter on wudu twice, p. 20 no. 137). In this hadith, fresh water is taken for each limb. In another hadith, he forbade bathing from janabah in a small amount of standing water. If there was no impurity on his body, the only reason for prohibition is that the water becomes used and cannot be used by others. Hence he forbade making water used by immersing in it. A hadith from Abu Hurayrah: The Messenger of Allah said, 'Let none of you bathe from janabah in standing water.' (d) (Muslim, chapter on prohibition of bathing in stagnant water, p. 138 no. 283). From these hadiths it is known that used water is pure but does not have purifying capacity. The author of al-Hidayah narrated several statements on the ruling of used water, but the correct view of the early imams is that it is pure but not purifying. As said in Mawsū'at al-Imam al-Shafi'i (chapter on ruling of used water, vol. 1 p. 52). (43) Used water: every water with which hadath has been removed, or used on the body as an act of devotion. (1) If actual impurity (najāsat 'ayniyya) is on the body or clothes and it is removed with water, that water is impure. But if there is no actual impurity, only major hadath (janabah) or minor hadath (wudu), the water used becomes used water. (2) Or if wudu was already present but wudu is performed again to gain closeness to Allah, this also becomes used water, the ruling of which has passed.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on used water (mā' musta'mal). It begins by defining used water: water that has been used to remove hadath (ritual impurity) whether ghusl or wudu, or water used on the body as an act of devotion (e.g., wudu for reward when already in wudu). The ruling: it is not permissible to use such water again for the same purpose because it lacks the capacity to purify. However, the water itself is pure (tāhir) but not purifying (tahūr). The author provides proofs: (1) the practice of the Companions who did not wash clothes wet with used water, indicating it is not impure; (2) the fact that Arabs in need did not use used water for wudu, indicating it is not purifying; (3) hadiths where the Prophet gave his used wudu water to the sick to drink, proving it is pure; (4) hadiths where the Prophet took fresh water for each limb, proving he did not consider used water purifying; (5) the prohibition of bathing in standing water while junub, lest one make the water used and spoil it for others. The author notes that the correct Hanafi view is that used water is pure but not purifying, citing al-Hidayah and al-Mawsū'a.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (mā' musta'mal): Water that has been used to remove ritual impurity (hadath) or used as an act of devotion on the body.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity, either minor (wudu) or major (ghusl), that prevents acts of worship.
طهور (tahūr): Water that is both pure and capable of purifying (i.e., can remove hadath or remove impurity).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on using water that was previously used for wudu to perform wudu again?
A) It is permissible because the water is pure.
B) It is not permissible because the water is impure.
C) It is not permissible because the water lacks purifying capacity.
D) It is permissible only if no other water is available.

Key Takeaway
Used water is legally pure (tāhir) but lacks the capacity to purify (tahūr), so it cannot be used for wudu or ghusl.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Ruling on Water Used for Purification (Ma' Musta'mal)
Ruling with proof on ma' musta'mal's purity and non-purifying nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ma' musta'mal and explain the hadith evidence for its purity and non-purifying nature.

Core Idea
Ma' musta'mal is pure but not purifying — it cannot be used for wudu or ghusl.

This lesson focuses on water that has been used for ritual purification, known as ma' musta'mal. The Hanafi school holds that such water remains pure (tahir) but loses its ability to purify (mutahir). We will examine the key hadith that support this nuanced position and contrast it with other views.

Guided Path
1
Define ma' musta'mal and state its hukm
Identify what water counts as musta'mal and what the Hanafi ruling is: it is pure (tahir) but not purifying (ghayr mutahir).
The definition includes removal of hadath or use on the body with intention of qurbah.
2
Analyze the hadith proving purity
Examine the narrations from Jabir and al-Sa'ib where the Prophet gave his wudu water to drink or poured it on someone. This shows the water is not impure.
If it were impure, the Prophet would not have given it.
3
Analyze the hadith proving it is not purifying
Look at the hadith where the Prophet used fresh water for each limb and the prohibition against bathing in stagnant water while in janabah. This indicates the used water cannot purify again.
If it were purifying, the Prophet would have reused it.
4
Contrast with opposing views and identify the mufta bihi
Note that some early Hanafis and other schools hold different views. The relied-upon position is the one stated in al-Hidayah: pure but not purifying.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Water that has been used (musta'mal) is not permissible to use for the purification of hadath (i.e., wudu or ghusl). (43) And water that has been used (musta'mal) is every water by which hadath is removed or which is used on the body with the intention of worship (qurbah). (44) There is a hadith from Jabir: 'The Messenger of Allah came to visit me while I was ill and unconscious. He performed wudu and poured the water of his wudu over me, and I regained consciousness.' (Bukhari, chapter on love of the Prophet, no. 193) And from al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid: 'My aunt took me to the Prophet and said, O Messenger of Allah, my sister's son has been afflicted (with madness). He wiped my head, prayed for blessings, then performed wudu, and I drank from the water of his wudu.' (Bukhari, chapter on using leftover wudu water, no. 19) From these hadith it is understood that ma' musta'mal is pure, otherwise the Prophet would not have given it to drink. Al-Bayhaqi also mentions many hadith on this. Those who argue it is not purifying cite hadith where the Prophet used fresh water for each limb. If ma' musta'mal were purifying, he would have reused it. For example, Ibn Abbas: 'Do you want to see how the Messenger of Allah performed wudu? He called for a vessel of water, took a handful, rinsed his mouth and nose, then took another handful, combined his hands, and washed his face...' (Abu Dawud, no. 137) And there is a prohibition against bathing in stagnant water while in a state of janabah. If there is no physical impurity, the only reason is that the water becomes musta'mal and cannot be used by others. So it is pure but not purifying. The author of al-Hidayah transmitted several opinions, but the correct view of the early imams is that it is pure but not purifying. (43) Ma' musta'mal is every water by which hadath is removed or used on the body with the intention of worship. If water is used to remove physical impurity from the body or clothes, it becomes impure. But if it is used only for hadath (minor or major) or for renewing wudu with the intention of drawing near to Allah, it becomes musta'mal. Footnotes: (a) The Prophet came to visit me... (b) al-Sa'ib's narration... (c) Ibn Abbas's demonstration... (d) Prohibition of bathing in stagnant water while in janabah. Then: or used on the body with the intention of qurbah (44).
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) regarding the status of water used for removing ritual impurity (hadath), known as ma' musta'mal. The author first states the ruling: such water cannot be used for purification from hadath. Then he defines ma' musta'mal: water used to remove hadath (minor or major) or applied to the body with the intention of drawing near to Allah (qurbah). He then provides evidence from hadith. The first set of hadith (from Jabir and al-Sa'ib) prove that the water left over from the Prophet's wudu is pure (tahir), because he gave it to others to drink or pour over them. This establishes that ma' musta'mal is not impure. The second set of hadith (from Ibn Abbas and the prohibition on bathing in stagnant water) prove that it is not purifying (tahir mutahir). If it were purifying, the Prophet would have reused the same water for multiple limbs, and the prohibition on bathing in stagnant water would not be justified. Thus, the Hanafi position is that ma' musta'mal is pure in itself but loses its purifying capability. The author notes that this is the relied-upon view (mu'tamad) of the early imams, as stated in al-Hidayah. The footnote (43) clarifies that water used for removing physical impurity (najis 'ayni) becomes impure, not musta'mal. The text ends with the repetition of the definition 'or used on the body with the intention of qurbah' leading into the next topic of tanned hides.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used to remove ritual impurity (hadath) or applied to the body with the intention of worship (qurbah).
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity, either minor (hadath asghar, requiring wudu) or major (hadath akbar, requiring ghusl).
قربة (qurbah): An act done with the intention of drawing near to Allah, such as wudu or ghusl for worship even if already in a state of purity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on water used for wudu (ma' musta'mal)?
A) It is impure (najis) and cannot be used for anything.
B) It is pure (tahir) and can be used for wudu again.
C) It is pure (tahir) but not purifying (ghayr mutahir), so it cannot be used for wudu or ghusl.
D) It is purifying (mutahir) but only for minor impurity.

Key Takeaway
Ma' musta'mal is a distinct Hanafi category: pure in substance but lacking the power to purify, based on prophetic practice and hadith evidence.

Ruling on Tanned Hides: Purification by Tanning
Ruling with proof on purification of hides by tanning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tanned hides, identify the exceptions (pig and human), and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Tanning purifies the hide of a dead animal, but pig and human skin remain impure.

This passage presents a clear ruling with proof on the purification of animal hides through tanning (dabgh). The matn declares that any tanned hide becomes pure (tahir), permitting its use for prayer and wudu. However, exceptions are made for pigskin, due to its essential impurity (najis al-'ayn), and human skin, out of respect for human dignity. The evidence comes from explicit hadith of the Prophet and a Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is tanning (dabgh) an animal hide. The ruling is that the hide becomes pure (tahir), allowing prayer on it and wudu from vessels made of it.
The ruling applies to all hides except those of pig and human.
2
Note the exceptions
Pigskin is excluded because the pig is considered najis al-'ayn (essentially impure) and cannot be purified by any process, based on Quran 6:145. Human skin is excluded due to the dignity and honor of humans.
These exceptions are explicit in the text.
3
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: 'Any hide that is tanned has become pure' (Nasa'i) and 'The tanning of a dead animal's hide is its purification' (Muslim). These establish that tanning removes impurities.
The hadith are ahad (single-chain) but their meaning is clear.
4
Understand the reasoning
Tanning extracts impure moisture and blood from the hide, leaving only the leather which is pure. The Arabs commonly used such vessels.
The prohibition on using hides in other hadith refers to untanned hides.
5
Apply the ruling
Any tanned hide from a permissible animal (not pig or human) is pure and can be used for prayer mats, water containers, etc.
This ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

And every hide that is tanned has become pure; prayer in it and wudu from it are permissible. (45) Except the skin of the pig and the human. (46) Benefit: Imam Muhammad said: If one performs wudu or ghusl with the intention of qurbah, the water becomes musta'mal; without qurbah, it does not. The water becomes musta'mal only when it separates from the limb. Before that, it cannot be considered musta'mal. Lexically, hadath means minor or major impurity; physical impurity is called najasah. The meaning of qurbah here is the intention to remove hadath or to perform wudu upon wudu. (44) Regarding the rulings of hides: When a raw hide is tanned, it becomes pure. Prayer is permissible on it, and wudu from its vessel is permissible. (1) When the hide of a dead animal is tanned, its impure moisture and flowing blood are removed, leaving only the leather, so it is pure. One can pray on it and perform wudu/ghusl from its vessel. The Arabs often used such vessels. (2) Hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah said, 'Any hide that is tanned has become pure.' (Nasa'i, no. 4246) Another hadith: 'The tanning of a dead animal's hide is its purification.' (Nasa'i and Muslim) These hadith indicate that after tanning, the hide of a dead animal becomes pure. The hadith that prohibit (using hides) refer to untanned hides. (45) However, the skin of the pig and of the human will not become pure. The pig is essentially impure (najis al-'ayn), so its hide does not become pure even after tanning. Allah says: 'or the flesh of the swine, for indeed it is impure' (6:145). And human skin is not permissible for use even after tanning due to its honor and dignity.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage contains the ruling on tanned hides (dabgh) and their purification. The matn states: any hide that is tanned becomes pure (tahir), and it is permissible to pray on it (e.g., a prayer mat) and to perform wudu from a vessel made of it. Then an exception: pigskin and human skin do not become pure through tanning. The commentary explains the reasoning: tanning removes the impure moisture and blood from the hide of a dead animal, leaving only the leather which is pure. This is supported by two hadith: 'Any hide that is tanned has become pure' and 'The tanning of a dead animal's hide is its purification.' These hadith establish that tanning purifies the hide. The text also clarifies that the prohibition against using hides refers to untanned hides. The exception for pigskin is because the pig is considered essentially impure (najis al-'ayn) in the Hanafi school, based on the Quranic verse calling it 'rijis'. Human skin is excluded out of respect for human dignity; it is not permissible to use human skin even if tanned. The passage also includes a tangential benefit (faa'idah) about the definition of ma' musta'mal, which seems to be a remnant from the previous lesson, but it is included in the text.

Key Terms
إهاب (ihab): Hide or skin of an animal, usually raw untanned.
دبغ (dabgh): Tanning process that purifies the hide by removing impurities.
نجس العين (najis al-'ayn): Something that is essentially impure, like the pig, whose impurity cannot be removed by any process.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following hides does NOT become pure through tanning?
A) Hide of a cow that died naturally.
B) Hide of a sheep that was slaughtered properly.
C) Hide of a pig.
D) Hide of a goat.

Key Takeaway
Tanning purifies the hide of dead animals, but pig (najis al-'ayn) and human (due to dignity) remain impure.

Ruling on Hair and Bones of a Dead Animal
Ruling with proof that hair and bones of dead animals are pure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hair and bones of a dead animal and explain the evidence from the hadith on ivory.

Core Idea
Hair and bones of dead animals are pure because they lack flowing blood, as proven by the Prophet's permission to use ivory.

In this lesson, we examine a distinctive Hanafi ruling: that hair, bones, hooves, and claws of a dead animal (maytah) are pure (tahir). While the meat and blood of a dead animal are impure (najis), these solid parts are an exception due to the absence of flowing blood. The primary evidence is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the purchase of ivory items for Fatimah, demonstrating that ivory from elephants—animals that are not Islamically slaughtered—is permissible and pure. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The passage rules that hair, bones, hooves, and claws of any dead animal (one that died without Islamic slaughter) are pure (tahir).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? A hadith from Thawban in Sunan Abi Dawud where the Prophet ordered to buy ivory items for Fatimah.
The hadith is ahad (single narration), so its transmission (thubut) is zanni, but its meaning (dalala) is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? Ivory comes from elephant tusks, and elephants are not slaughtered Islamically; yet the Prophet allowed its use. This indicates that bones (and by analogy, hair, hooves, etc.) of dead animals are pure.
The Hanafi principle: parts without flowing blood are not impure.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Yes, the Shafi'i school generally holds that all parts of a dead animal are impure. The Hanafis respond by distinguishing based on the absence of flowing blood.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
