وشعر الميتة وعظمها طاهر (۱) بال ، ہڈی ، کھر اور سیٹنگ میں بہتا ہوا خوان نہیں ہوتا ہے اور نہ ناپاک رطوبت ہوتی ہے اس لئے مردار کی یہ چیزیں بھی پاک ہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے قال رسول الله الله يا ثوبان اشتر لفاطمة قلادة من عصب وسوارين من عاج (ب)(ابوداؤد شریف، باب في الانتفاع بالعاج جلد ثانی ص ۲۲۷ نمبر ۴۲۱۳) اول کتاب الخاتم سے پہلے ہے۔ حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مردار جانور کا ٹھہ بھی پاک ہے اور ہاتھی کے دانت بھی پاک ہیں۔ ورنہ آپ پٹھے کا ہار اور ہاتھی دانت کا کنگن خریدنے کے لئے کیسے فرماتے ۔ حاشیہ : (ب) آپ نے فرمایا کہ اے ثوبان فاطمہ کے لئے بچھے کا ہار اور ہاتھی دانت کے دو کنگن خریدو۔
And the hair of a dead animal and its bone are pure. (1) Hair, bones, hooves, and claws do not contain flowing blood nor impure moisture, therefore these parts of a dead animal are also pure. (2) The Messenger of Allah said: 'O Thawban, buy for Fatimah a necklace of 'asb (ivory) and two bracelets of ivory.' (Abu Dawud, no. 4213) This hadith indicates that the ivory (tusks) of a dead animal are pure, and also elephant tusks are pure. Otherwise, the Prophet would not have ordered to buy a necklace of ivory and bracelets of ivory. Footnote (b): He said: 'O Thawban, buy for Fatimah a necklace of 'asb and two bracelets of ivory.'
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage rules that the hair and bones of a dead animal (that died without Islamic slaughter) are pure (tahir). The reasoning is that these parts do not contain flowing blood or impure moisture; they are solid and not considered impure by nature. This is a Hanafi position that distinguishes between parts that have blood flow (like meat, organs) and those that do not (like hair, bones, hooves). The proof is a hadith where the Prophet ordered the purchase of ivory items for Fatimah. Ivory comes from elephant tusks, and elephants are not slaughtered Islamically; yet the Prophet approved its use, indicating that such parts are pure. This ruling applies to all similar parts of dead animals, including hair and bones. The footnote clarifies the hadith.

Key Terms
ميتة (maytah): An animal that died without proper Islamic slaughter.
عظم (azm): Bone, including ivory and similar hard parts.
عاج (aj): Ivory, specifically elephant tusk, used as evidence for purity of bones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on hair from a dead animal?
A) It is impure and cannot be used.
B) It is pure if the animal was slaughtered Islamically.
C) It is pure because it contains no flowing blood.
D) It is purifying (mutahir) for wudu.

Key Takeaway
Hair and bones of dead animals are pure and can be used, as established by the hadith on ivory and the absence of impure blood.

Taharah — Purification
beginner

Tanning Hides: The Hanafi Ruling and Its Exceptions
Ruling with proof on hide tanning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that tanning (dibagh) purifies the hide of a dead animal in Hanafi law, identify the two exceptions (pig and human), and cite the supporting hadith.

Core Idea
Tanning transforms a dead animal's impure hide into a pure material for use.

The Hanafi school holds that tanning (dibagh) removes the impurities from the hide of a dead animal, rendering it pure and permissible for prayer and wudu. This ruling is based on clear prophetic traditions. However, there are two crucial exceptions: pig and human. In this lesson, we will examine the evidence and the reasoning behind these exceptions.

Guided Path
1
State the main ruling
Identify the core claim: tanning purifies any hide. Note that the passage explicitly says 'Every hide that is tanned becomes pure'.
2
Identify the exceptions
Find the two exceptions stated: pig and human. Understand why pig is excluded (najis al-'ayn from Quran) and human (dignity).
3
Locate the primary evidence
Extract the hadith cited: from Ibn Abbas, 'Any hide that is tanned becomes pure' and 'The slaughter of the sheep is its tanning'. Note these are found in Sunan al-Nasa'i and Muslim.
4
Address the prohibition hadith
Understand that the hadith prohibiting use of hide refers to untanned hide, reconciling the apparent conflict.

Every hide that is tanned becomes pure, so prayer in it and wudu from it are permissible. Except the skin of pig and human. The hair of a dead animal and its bone are pure. Benefit: Imam Muhammad says: if one performs wudu or ghusl with the intention of drawing near (to Allah), the water becomes used (musta'mal). If used without intention, it does not become used. Used water is when it separates from the limb. Before that, it is not considered used. Lexically, hadath: minor hadath like wudu, major hadath like janabah. 'Ayni najasah is called najasah. Wajh al-qurbah: intention to remove hadath or intention to perform wudu over wudu. Ruling of hides: Raw hide, if tanned, becomes pure. Prayer in it and wudu from its vessel are permissible. (1) If the hide of a dead animal is tanned, its impure moisture and flowing blood are removed, leaving only the hide, so it is pure. One can pray on it and perform wudu or ghusl from its vessel. The Arabs often had such vessels. (2) Hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Any hide that is tanned becomes pure.' (Nasai, Bab Jilud al-Maytah, vol. 2, p. 69, no. 4246). Another hadith: 'The slaughter of the sheep is its tanning.' (Nasai, Bab Jilud al-Maytah, p. 169, no. 425; Muslim, Bab Taharah Jilud al-Maytah bi al-Dibagh, p. 157, no. 366). From these hadith, it is known that after tanning, the hide of a dead animal becomes pure. The hadith that prohibits refers to untanned hide. (45) But pig skin and human skin will not become pure. Pig is najis al-'ayn, so its hide will not be pure even after tanning. The verse: 'or the flesh of pig, for that is impure' (al-An'am 6:145). Human skin is not usable due to dignity and honor even after tanning. (46) The hair and bone of a dead animal are pure. (1) Hair, bone, hoof, and sinew do not contain flowing blood nor impure moisture, so these parts of a dead animal are also pure. (2) Hadith: The Messenger of Allah said: 'O Thawban, buy for Fatimah a necklace of sinew and two bracelets of ivory.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Intifa' bi al-'Aaj, vol. 2, p. 227, no. 4213). From this hadith, it is known that the sinew of a dead animal is pure, and elephant tusks are pure. Otherwise, how would he command to buy a necklace of sinew and ivory bracelets? Footnote: (a) If a raw hide is tanned, it becomes pure. (b) He said: O Thawban, buy for Fatimah a necklace of sinew and two bracelets of ivory. Then, Imam Shafi'i says that everything except the skin is impure. Their evidence is this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Ukaym: 'The Messenger of Allah wrote to us: Do not benefit from the hide or sinew of a dead animal.' (Nasai, Bab ma yadbagh bihi jild al-maytah, vol. 2, p. 170, no. 4255; Ibn Majah, Bab man kana la yantafi'u min al-maytah bi ihab wa la 'asab, p. 520, no. 3613; Daraqutni, Bab al-Dibagh, vol. 1, p. 42, no. 113). The Hanafis argue using the hadith of Abu Dawud which permits use of sinew and ivory. Umm Salamah said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'There is no harm in the skin of a dead animal if tanned, and no harm in its wool, hair, and horns if washed with water.' (Daraqutni, Bab al-Dibagh, no. 113). From this hadith, it is known that bone, horn, and hair are pure. Principle: Bones that do not contain flowing blood are pure.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on the purity of animal parts after death. The author begins by stating the ruling that tanning (dibagh) purifies any hide, making it permissible to pray on it or perform wudu from its container. This is a well-established ruling supported by multiple hadith, including the famous 'any hide that is tanned becomes pure' from Ibn Abbas. The rule applies to all animals except two: pig and human. Pig is excluded because it is intrinsically impure (najis al-'ayn) as per Quranic verse; human skin is excluded due to the inherent dignity of humans. 

The passage then addresses the purity of hair, bones, and sinew of dead animals. The Hanafi school holds these to be pure (tahir) because they do not contain flowing blood or impure moisture. Evidence is drawn from the hadith of Thawban where the Prophet commanded buying a sinew necklace and ivory bracelets for Fatimah, indicating that these items are pure. The author also cites a principle: bones without flowing blood are pure. 

The passage then engages with the Shafi'i objection. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that everything except the skin of a dead animal is impure, relying on the hadith of Abdullah ibn Ukaym prohibiting benefit from hide or sinew. The Hanafi response reconciles the conflicting hadith by noting that the prohibition applies to untanned hide and sinew, while tanning removes impurity. Furthermore, the hadith of Umm Salamah explicitly permits wool, hair, and horns after washing, which are not tanned but washed. Thus, the Hanafi position is that tanning purifies hides, and washing purifies hair, bones, and sinew. The overall ruling is based on ease and authentic evidence.

Key Terms
اهاب (ihab): Raw, untanned hide or skin of an animal.
دبغ (dabgh): Tanning process that removes impurities and purifies the hide.
رجس (rijs): Impurity, filth. Used in Quran for pig.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the skin of a pig after tanning?
A) It becomes pure and can be used.
B) It remains impure because pig is najis al-'ayn.
C) It becomes pure only if the pig was slaughtered.
D) It becomes pure but cannot be used for prayer.

Key Takeaway
Tanning purifies the hide of any dead animal except pig (intrinsically impure) and human (due to dignity).

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Purity of Hair, Bones, and Sinew of Dead Animals: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on non-skin parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that hair, bones, and sinew of dead animals are pure after washing, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Hair, bones, and sinew of dead animals are pure because they lack flowing blood, and explicit hadith confirms their permissibility.

After discussing tanning hides, the passage turns to other parts of a dead animal: hair, bones, and sinew. The Hanafi school declares these pure after washing, citing the hadith of Thawban and Umm Salamah. The Shafi'i school disagrees, relying on a hadith that prohibits benefiting from hide and sinew. This lesson will dissect the arguments and show how the Hanafis reconcile the texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi claim
The passage states that hair, bone, hoof, and sinew of a dead animal are pure and can be used after washing.
Note the principle: parts without flowing blood are not impure.
2
Locate the Hanafi evidence
Find the two hadith: (a) Prophet's command to buy a sinew necklace and ivory bracelets for Fatimah. (b) Hadith of Umm Salamah explicitly permitting wool, hair, and horns after washing.
These are found in Abu Dawud and Daraqutni.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i uses the hadith of Abdullah ibn Ukaym: 'Do not benefit from hide or sinew of a dead animal.' This appears to prohibit sinew.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds by reconciling: the prohibition applies to untanned hide and sinew; tanning and washing remove impurity. The permission in Umm Salamah's hadith is more specific and thus takes precedence.
Also, the sinew in the necklace was presumably tanned or washed.
5
Derive the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis can use hair brushes, bone handles, sinew threads from dead animals after washing; Shafi'is consider them impure and avoid them.

باهاب ولا عصب (الف) (نسائی شریف، باب ماید بغ به جلو المیت ج ثانی ص۱۷۰ نمبر ۴۲۵۵ رابین ماجہ شریف ، باب من كان لا ينتفعو امن المبيته باهاب ولا عصب، ص ۵۲۰، نمبر ۳۶۱۳ / دار قطنی ، باب الدباغة ج اول ص ۴۲ نمبر ۱۱۳) حنفیہ ابو داؤ د والی حدیث سے استدلال کرتے ہیں جس میں بیٹھے اور ہاتھی دانت سے استفادہ کی اجازت معلوم ہوتی ہے۔ سمعت ام سلمة تقول سمعت رسول الله الا الله يقول لا بأس بمسك الميتة اذا دبغ ولا بأس بصوفها وشعرها وقرونها اذا غسل مالماء (ب) (دارقطنی ، باب الدباغتہ ،نمبر۱۱۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہڈی ، سینگ اور بال پاک ہیں۔ اصول جن ہڈیوں میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہے وہ پاک ہے۔ اهاب : کچا چمڑا، دباغت دیئے بغیر کا چمڑا۔
Every hide that is tanned becomes pure, so prayer in it and wudu from it are permissible. Except the skin of pig and human. The hair of a dead animal and its bone are pure. Benefit: Imam Muhammad says: if one performs wudu or ghusl with the intention of drawing near (to Allah), the water becomes used (musta'mal). If used without intention, it does not become used. Used water is when it separates from the limb. Before that, it is not considered used. Lexically, hadath: minor hadath like wudu, major hadath like janabah. 'Ayni najasah is called najasah. Wajh al-qurbah: intention to remove hadath or intention to perform wudu over wudu. Ruling of hides: Raw hide, if tanned, becomes pure. Prayer in it and wudu from its vessel are permissible. (1) If the hide of a dead animal is tanned, its impure moisture and flowing blood are removed, leaving only the hide, so it is pure. One can pray on it and perform wudu or ghusl from its vessel. The Arabs often had such vessels. (2) Hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Any hide that is tanned becomes pure.' (Nasai, Bab Jilud al-Maytah, vol. 2, p. 69, no. 4246). Another hadith: 'The slaughter of the sheep is its tanning.' (Nasai, Bab Jilud al-Maytah, p. 169, no. 425; Muslim, Bab Taharah Jilud al-Maytah bi al-Dibagh, p. 157, no. 366). From these hadith, it is known that after tanning, the hide of a dead animal becomes pure. The hadith that prohibits refers to untanned hide. (45) But pig skin and human skin will not become pure. Pig is najis al-'ayn, so its hide will not be pure even after tanning. The verse: 'or the flesh of pig, for that is impure' (al-An'am 6:145). Human skin is not usable due to dignity and honor even after tanning. (46) The hair and bone of a dead animal are pure. (1) Hair, bone, hoof, and sinew do not contain flowing blood nor impure moisture, so these parts of a dead animal are also pure. (2) Hadith: The Messenger of Allah said: 'O Thawban, buy for Fatimah a necklace of sinew and two bracelets of ivory.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Intifa' bi al-'Aaj, vol. 2, p. 227, no. 4213). From this hadith, it is known that the sinew of a dead animal is pure, and elephant tusks are pure. Otherwise, how would he command to buy a necklace of sinew and ivory bracelets? Footnote: (a) If a raw hide is tanned, it becomes pure. (b) He said: O Thawban, buy for Fatimah a necklace of sinew and two bracelets of ivory. Then, Imam Shafi'i says that everything except the skin is impure. Their evidence is this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Ukaym: 'The Messenger of Allah wrote to us: Do not benefit from the hide or sinew of a dead animal.' (Nasai, Bab ma yadbagh bihi jild al-maytah, vol. 2, p. 170, no. 4255; Ibn Majah, Bab man kana la yantafi'u min al-maytah bi ihab wa la 'asab, p. 520, no. 3613; Daraqutni, Bab al-Dibagh, vol. 1, p. 42, no. 113). The Hanafis argue using the hadith of Abu Dawud which permits use of sinew and ivory. Umm Salamah said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'There is no harm in the skin of a dead animal if tanned, and no harm in its wool, hair, and horns if washed with water.' (Daraqutni, Bab al-Dibagh, no. 113). From this hadith, it is known that bone, horn, and hair are pure. Principle: Bones that do not contain flowing blood are pure.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on the purity of animal parts after death. The author begins by stating the ruling that tanning (dibagh) purifies any hide, making it permissible to pray on it or perform wudu from its container. This is a well-established ruling supported by multiple hadith, including the famous 'any hide that is tanned becomes pure' from Ibn Abbas. The rule applies to all animals except two: pig and human. Pig is excluded because it is intrinsically impure (najis al-'ayn) as per Quranic verse; human skin is excluded due to the inherent dignity of humans. 

The passage then addresses the purity of hair, bones, and sinew of dead animals. The Hanafi school holds these to be pure (tahir) because they do not contain flowing blood or impure moisture. Evidence is drawn from the hadith of Thawban where the Prophet commanded buying a sinew necklace and ivory bracelets for Fatimah, indicating that these items are pure. The author also cites a principle: bones without flowing blood are pure. 

The passage then engages with the Shafi'i objection. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that everything except the skin of a dead animal is impure, relying on the hadith of Abdullah ibn Ukaym prohibiting benefit from hide or sinew. The Hanafi response reconciles the conflicting hadith by noting that the prohibition applies to untanned hide and sinew, while tanning removes impurity. Furthermore, the hadith of Umm Salamah explicitly permits wool, hair, and horns after washing, which are not tanned but washed. Thus, the Hanafi position is that tanning purifies hides, and washing purifies hair, bones, and sinew. The overall ruling is based on ease and authentic evidence.

Key Terms
عصب ('asab): Sinew or tendon of an animal.
عاج ('aj): Ivory, specifically elephant tusk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith does the Hanafi school use to support the purity of hair and wool from dead animals?
A) The hadith of Thawban about the necklace of sinew.
B) The hadith of Ibn Ukaym prohibiting sinew.
C) The hadith of Umm Salamah mentioning wool, hair, and horns after washing.
D) The hadith 'Any hide that is tanned becomes pure.'

Key Takeaway
Hair, bones, sinew, and horns of dead animals are pure after washing, based on explicit hadith and the absence of flowing blood.

Purification of a Well When Impurity Falls into It
Ruling on removing water from a well when impurity falls in, with conditions and ease of practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on purifying a well when an impurity falls into it, including the conditions that affect whether the entire well must be emptied.

Core Idea
Emptying all water from a small well is wajib; large wells become impure only with frequent impurity.

In this passage, the author explains the ruling on wells contaminated by impurity, distinguishing between small and large wells and highlighting the principle of ease (rukhsah) due to hardship. You will see how a Companion's action provides the evidence for this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is purification of a well when impurity falls in. The ruling is that the water must be emptied (nazh) and that emptying is itself the purification.
The ruling is wajib.
2
Determine the conditions
The size of the well and the type/frequency of impurity affect whether the well becomes impure. Small wells become impure entirely; large wells like ponds do not with small impurities. Also, frequent impurity (e.g., dung) renders the well impure after many occurrences, while occasional impurities (e.g., a drop of blood) do not.
Differentiate between small and large wells.
3
Note the easing (rukhsah) and its basis
The Shariah provides ease: walls and mud are purified simply by removing water, without separate washing. This is due to hardship and is not based on analogical reasoning (qiyas).
This concession is specific to wells.
4
Trace the dalil and its implication
The evidence is from Ata: an Ethiopian fell into Zamzam and died, and Ibn al-Zubayr ordered that its water be emptied. This indicates that the entire well becomes impure and must be emptied. The hadith is recorded by Tahawi and Daraqutni.
The action of a Companion is taken as proof.

Source Text

(47) And if an impurity falls into a well, it is to be emptied, and the emptying of its water is its purification. It has passed earlier that if the well is like a large pond, it does not become impure by a small impurity falling. But if the length and width of the well are small, the impurity will move from one side to the other and descend into the depths, so the entire well becomes impure. Since emptying all the water of the well is difficult, therefore for a well in the desert or forest where impurity frequently falls, such as dung, etc., it will become impure by many fallings. And impurity that occurs occasionally, like blood, one drop falling does not make the well impure. Similarly, if the wall of the well becomes impure from impure water, it is difficult to wash it, so there is no need to wash it; simply removing the water will purify the wall. Similarly, mud and remaining water need not be removed; they will become pure by removing the water. This ease is given by the Shariah due to necessity. Therefore, analogy has no place here. The evidence for the entire well becoming impure is from Ata: that an Ethiopian fell into Zamzam and died, and Ibn al-Zubayr ordered that its water be emptied. (Tahawi, Bab al-Ma' taqa'u fihi al-najasah, p. 26; Daraqutni, Bab al-Bi'r idha awqa'a fihi hayawan, p. 28, no. 62). From this hadith, it is known that from the death of a human, the entire well becomes impure. Similarly, from impurity falling, the entire well...
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage discusses the purification of a well when an impurity falls into it. The author begins with the ruling: if impurity falls into a well, the water must be emptied, and the act of emptying is itself the purification. This is because the well is a confined space, and the impurity disperses throughout. However, earlier it was noted that if the well is large like a pond, a small impurity does not render it impure. For small wells, the impurity spreads, so the entire water becomes impure. The author then addresses practical difficulties: in the desert or forest where impurity like dung frequently falls, the well becomes impure only after many occurrences; occasional impurities like a drop of blood do not make it impure. An important point of ease: if the well's walls become impure, they do not need to be washed separately; simply removing the water purifies them. Similarly, mud and leftover water are purified by emptying. This is a concession from Shariah due to hardship, and it is not based on analogy (qiyas). The evidence is the action of Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr when an Ethiopian died in Zamzam; he ordered the entire well to be emptied, indicating that the whole well becomes impure. This ruling applies to any impurity causing the well to become impure.

Key Terms
نزح (nazh): To empty or bail out water from a well completely.
بئر (bi'r): A well, typically a confined source of water.
نجاسة (najasah): An impurity, such as blood, dung, or a dead body, that falls into water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Purifying the water with chemicals

Key Takeaway
A small well becomes impure when impurity falls in, and must be purified by emptying all water; this is based on the practice of the Companion Ibn al-Zubayr.

The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Purification of Dead Animal Parts
Inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i on impurity of dead animal body parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the purity of dead animal parts (hide, hair, bones, horns) and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Tanning purifies the hide; hair, bones, and horns are pure by default — not all dead animal parts are equally impure.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only the hide can be purified through tanning, while all other parts remain impure. The Hanafi school, based on a hadith from Umm Salamah, argues that tanning purifies the hide and that hair, bones, and horns are pure even without tanning. Understanding the proofs on both sides will sharpen your ability to weigh conflicting hadith evidences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafis hold that hide becomes pure through tanning, and hair, bones, and horns are pure (if washed). Identify the exact ruling for each part.
The hide requires tanning; the other parts only require washing.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that only hide is purifiable; other parts remain impure. Note which parts are specifically disputed (sinews, bones, etc.).
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
They cite the hadith of Abdullah ibn Ukaym prohibiting use of hide and sinews. Examine the wording and its implications.
Hadith: 'Do not benefit from the dead animal's hide nor its sinews.'
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis counter with the hadith of Umm Salamah which explicitly allows hide after tanning and hair/bones after washing. Explain how this hadith is considered more specific.
Hadith: 'There is no harm in the hide... if tanned, and no harm in its wool, hair, and horns if washed with water.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: Hanafis permit using tanned hide and consider hair/bones pure; Shafi'is only permit using tanned hide.
This impacts everyday use: e.g., using leather from dead animals, using bones for tools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Then Imam al-Shafi'i says everything except hide is impure. Their proof is this hadith: From Abdullah ibn Ukaym: The Messenger of Allah wrote to us: 'Do not benefit from the dead animal's hide nor its sinews.' (Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, Dar Qutni) The Hanafis use the hadith from Abu Dawud which indicates the permissibility of benefiting from ivory and elephant tusk. I heard Umm Salamah say: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'There is no harm in the hide of a dead animal if tanned, and there is no harm in its wool, hair, and horns if washed with water.' (Dar Qutni) From this hadith it becomes known that bone, horn, and hair are pure. Principle: bones that do not contain flowing blood are pure. Ihab: raw hide, untanned hide.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only the hide of a dead animal can be purified through tanning; all other parts (sinews, bones, etc.) remain impure. His proof is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Ukaym prohibiting use of hide and sinews. The Hanafis argue that tanning purifies the hide, and additionally, hair, bones, and horns are pure by default based on the hadith of Umm Salamah. The hadith of Umm Salamah explicitly mentions the purity of hide after tanning and the purity of wool, hair, and horns after washing. The Hanafi principle: any bone without flowing blood is pure. The term 'ihab' is defined as raw, untanned hide.

Key Terms
اهاب (ihab): Raw, untanned hide of a dead animal

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tanning purifies the hide; hair, bones, and horns are pure by default — a key Hanafi distinction in taharah.

Purification of a Well When Impurity Falls In
General ruling on well purification with exceptions and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for purifying a well when impurity falls in, identify the proof, and distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the minimum quantity of water.

Core Idea
Impurity in a well requires removal of all water; but necessity and istihsan modify the rule for large wells and frequent impurities.

When impurity enters a well, the default Hanafi ruling is that the entire well becomes impure and must be emptied. However, the fuqaha introduced exceptions based on the size of the well and the frequency of impurity, all grounded in the principle of istihsan. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its dalil, and the contrasting Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the falling of impurity into a well. The ruling is that the water must be removed (nazh) – this removal is itself the purification (taharah).
The ruling applies to wells that are not as large as ponds.
2
Understand the exceptions
Two exceptions: (1) Large wells (like ponds) do not become impure from a small impurity. (2) For small wells, occasional impurities (e.g., one drop of blood) do not render the well impure; only frequent impurities (e.g., dung) cause impurity after many falls.
Also, the walls and mud become pure by merely removing the water, due to hardship.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The proof is from the incident of Zamzam: an Ethiopian fell in and died, and Ibn Zubayr ordered the water removed. This action indicates that death (and by analogy, impurity) renders the entire well impure.
The hadith is mursal (zanni al-thubut) but its implication (dalala) is considered qat'i.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Shafi'i
Imam Shafi'i holds that a well with two qullas (approx. 200 litres) does not become impure unless colour, taste, or smell changes. His proof is the hadith of qullatayn.
The Hanafi school differentiates based on well size and impurity type, not solely on water quantity.
5
Recognize the role of istihsan
The concessions (e.g., not requiring washing of walls) are based on necessity (hardship) and are outside the scope of qiyas. Istihsan overrides strict analogy.
This is a clear example of istihsan in taharah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۷) واذا وقعت فى البئر نجاسة نزحت و كان نزح ما فيها من الماء طهارة لها. کنویں کے مسائل کے ( ۴۷ ) اگر کنویں میں ناپا کی گر جائے تو اس کا پانی نکالا جائے گا۔ اور جو اس میں پانی ہے اس کا نکالنا ہی اس کا پاک ہونا ہے۔ ر پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ بڑے تالاب کی طرح کنواں ہو تو وہ تھوڑی نجاست گرنے سے ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن کنویں کی لمبائی اور چوڑائی کم ہوتو نا پا کی ایک کنارے سے دوسرے کنارے کی طرف چلی جائے گی اور نا پا کی نیچے اتر اتر کر گہرائی کی طرف چلی جائے گی اس لئے پورا کنواں ناپاک ہو جائے گا۔ پورے کنویں کا پانی بار بار نکالنا مشکل ہے اس لئے صحرا اور جنگل میں جو نجاست بار بار کنویں میں گرتی ہے مثلا گو بر ۔ لید وغیرہ تو اس کے بہت سے گرنے سے ناپاک ہوگا ۔ اور جو نجاست کبھی کبھار کرتی ہے جیسے خون تو اس کا ایک قطرہ گرنے سے کنواں ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ اسی طرح نا پاک پانی سے کنویں کی دیوار ناپاک ہوگی لیکن اس کو دھونا مشکل ہے اس لئے اس کو دھونے کی ضرورت نہیں صرف پانی نکالنے سے دیوار پاک ہو جائے گی۔ اسی طرح کیچڑ اور باقی ماندہ پانی بھی نکالنے کی ضرورت نہیں وہ بھی پانی نکالنے سے پاک ہو جائیں گے۔ یہ سہولت مجبوری کی بنا پر شریعت نے دی ہے۔ اس لئے اس میں قیاس کو دخل نہیں ہے۔ پورا کنواں ناپاک ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے عن عطاء ان حبشيا وقع في زمزم فمات فامر ابن الزبير فنزح مانها (ج) ( طحاوی شریف ، باب الماء تقع فيه النجاسته ۲۶ ردار قطنی ، باب البئر از اوقع فیها حیوان ص ۲۸ نمبر ۶۲ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ انسان کے مرنے سے پورا کنواں نا پاک ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح ناپاکی گرنے سے پورا کنواں : فائی امام شافعی کا مسلک گذر گیا ہے کہ دو مٹکے کنویں میں پانی ہو تو جب تک اوصاف ثلاثہ میں سے ایک نہ بدلے ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ دلیل حدیث قلتین گزرگئی۔ ان نزح : پانی کا کنواں سے نکالنا۔
(47) And if impurity falls into the well, it is emptied, and the emptying of its water is purification for it. (47) If impurity falls into the well, its water is removed. The removal of that water is its purification. It has passed before that if the well is like a large pond, it does not become impure by a small impurity falling. But if the length and width of the well are small, the impurity will move from one side to the other and descend to the depth, so the entire well becomes impure. Removing the water of the entire well repeatedly is difficult, so in deserts and forests where impurities frequently fall into the well (e.g., dung, etc.), many falls cause impurity. But for impurities that occur occasionally, like blood, one drop does not make the well impure. Similarly, if the wall of the well becomes impure from impure water, washing it is difficult, so it does not need washing; only removing water purifies the wall. Similarly, mud and remaining water do not need to be removed; they become pure by removing water. This concession is given by the Shariah due to necessity, so analogy does not apply here. The proof for the entire well becoming impure is from Ata: an Ethiopian fell into Zamzam and died, and Ibn Zubayr ordered that its water be removed. (Tahawi, Dar Qutni) From this hadith it is known that the death of a human makes the entire well impure. Similarly, impurity falling makes the entire well impure. The position of Imam Shafi'i has passed: if there is two qullas of water in the well, it does not become impure unless one of the three attributes changes. The proof of the hadith of qullatayn has passed. An-nazh: removal of water from the well.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage states the general ruling for purifying a well when impurity falls into it. The method is to remove all the water; the removal itself is the purification. The author then discusses exceptions: large wells (like ponds) do not become impure from small amounts of impurity. Small wells become entirely impure because impurity spreads throughout. There is a concession for frequently occurring impurities (like dung in desert wells) where many falls are needed to make it impure; occasional impurities like a drop of blood do not make it impure. The walls and mud are purified by simply removing the water, due to hardship. The textual proof is the incident at Zamzam where the entire well was emptied after a person died in it. The passage also notes that Imam al-Shafi'i differs: he holds that a well with two qullas of water (approximately 200 liters) does not become impure unless its color, taste, or smell changes, based on the hadith of qullatayn.

Key Terms
نزح (nazh): Removal of water from a well as a method of purification
قلتان (qullatayn): Two qullas (approximately 200 litres) – the minimum quantity of water that does not become impure unless attributes change according to Shafi'i.
اوصاف ثلاثہ (awsaf thalatha): The three attributes (colour, taste, smell) whose change indicates impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, which type of impurity does NOT make a small well impure?
A) A dead animal falling into the well.
B) A single drop of blood falling into the well.
C) Urine that has been spilled into the well.
D) A large amount of dung that falls repeatedly.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on well purification balances default impurity (najis) with concessions due to hardship, using istihsan and the Zamzam incident as core proof.

Ruling for Medium Animals in a Well: 40-50 Buckets
Specific ruling on water removal for medium animals in a well

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for medium-sized animals dying in a well (40-50 buckets) and identify the proof from the statement of al-Sha'bi.

Core Idea
Medium animals require 40-50 buckets of water removal, as per tabi'i statement.

In Hanafi fiqh, the size of an animal that falls into a well determines the amount of water that must be removed. This lesson focuses on medium-sized animals like pigeons, chickens, and cats. You will learn the specific ruling and the proof behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animal size category
The passage classifies animals as small, medium, or large. Here, the animals listed (pigeon, chicken, cat) are medium. Confirm this categorization.
2
Recall the required quantity
For medium animals, between 40 and 50 buckets of water must be removed from the well. Memorize this range.
The minimum is 40; the maximum is 50. The exact number may vary based on size.
3
Locate the proof
The ruling is based on the statement of al-Sha'bi, a tabi'i, who said to remove 40 buckets. This is a qawl sahabi-like evidence, though al-Sha'bi is a tabi'i.
4
Understand the range
The text gives a range (40-50). This accounts for differences in animal size and scholarly opinion. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) is 40-50 buckets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۹) وان ماتت فيها حمامة او دجاجة او سنور نزح منها ما بين اربعين دلوا الى خمسين (۴۹) اور اگر کنویں میں کبوتر یا مرغی بابلی مرجائے تو کنویں سے چالیس سے پچاس ڈول تک نکالے جائیں گے (1) عن الشعبي في الطير والسنور ونحوهما يقع في البئر قال نزح منها اربعون دلوا (ب) (طحاوی شریف، باب الماء تقع فيه النجاسة ص ٦ ا ر مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب البئر تقع فيه الدابة ج اول نمبر ۲۷۲ / مصنف ابن ابی هیته نمبر ۱۷۱۲)

From al-Sha'bi regarding a bird, cat, and similar falling into a well: he said, 'Remove forty buckets.' (Tahawi, Abdurrazzaq, Ibn Abi Shayba)

This passage provides the ruling for medium-sized animals such as a pigeon, chicken, or cat. When such animals die in a well, between 40 and 50 buckets of water must be removed. The proof is the statement of al-Sha'bi (a tabi'i) who said to remove 40 buckets. The range of 40-50 likely accounts for differences in size and the opinion that 40 is the minimum and 50 is recommended.

Ruling for Large Animals Falling into a Well
Ruling on total water removal for large animals in a well

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a large animal (dog, sheep, human) dies in a well and cite the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
If a large animal dies in a well, all water must be removed — impurity spreads entirely.

This passage addresses a specific case in taharah: what happens when a large animal dies in a well. The Hanafi school mandates total removal of water, unlike smaller animals. We will examine the ruling, its evidence, and a cross-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the death of a large animal (dog, sheep, or human) in a well. The ruling is obligatory removal of all water.
Large animals are defined as those whose bodies are sizeable enough to spread impurity throughout the well.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: the incident of an Ethiopian dying in Zamzam requiring total removal, and a hadith from Ata stating 'If a dog falls into the well, remove (water) from it.'
The hadith is mursal (from a tabi'i directly) but accepted in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'أخرج' (remove) implies complete removal because the dog is a large animal; the Zamzam incident confirms total removal for humans.
The underlying rationale is that a large carcass contaminates the entire well water.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that water need only be removed if its properties (color, taste, smell) change; otherwise, the well remains pure.
Hanafi position is based on the generality of the evidence, while Shafi'i restrict it.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi ruling is mufta bihi within the school, based on the strength of the practice and the hadith.
Later Hanafi works confirm total removal as the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۰) وان مات فيها كلب او شاة او آدمي نزح ما فيها كله (۵۰) اور اگر کنویں میں کتا یا بکری یا آدمی مر جائے تو تمام پانی نکالا جائے۔ (۱) یہ جانور بڑے ہوتے ہیں اس کے مرتے ہی پورے کنویں میں نجاست پھیل جائے گی اس لئے پورے کنویں کا پانی نکالا جائے گا (۲) او پر حدیث گزری کہ زمزم کے کنویں میں حبشی مراتو پورا کنواں نکالا گیا (۳) عن عطاء قال اذا سقط الكلب في البئر فاخرج منها
(50) And if a dog, sheep, or human dies in it, remove all of its water. (50) And if a dog, goat, or human dies in the well, all water is removed. (1) These animals are large; upon their death, impurity spreads throughout the entire well, so all water must be removed. (2) The hadith has passed that when an Ethiopian died in Zamzam, all water was removed. (3) From Ata: 'If a dog falls into the well, remove (water) from it.'
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage addresses large animals: a dog, sheep, or human. When such a large animal dies in a well, all water must be removed because the body is large enough to spread impurity throughout the entire well. The proof is the incident of the Ethiopian dying in Zamzam, which required total removal. Additionally, a hadith from Ata mentions removing water when a dog falls in, though the full text is not quoted here but understood from context.

Well Purification: Small Animals (20-30 Buckets)
Ruling on number of buckets to draw for small dead animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of buckets to draw when a small animal dies in a well and apply the condition of bucket size and bloating.

Core Idea
A small dead animal in a well requires 20–30 buckets drawn, adjusted for bucket size; bloating changes the rule to emptying the entire well.

This passage from the Hanafi matn addresses a common scenario: a small animal like a mouse or sparrow falls into a well and dies. The ruling specifies a range of buckets to draw, emphasizing that the number depends on bucket size. The author also clarifies the distinction when the animal is bloated, citing a hadith from Ali (ra) that is interpreted accordingly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals and the act
Recognize the listed small animals (mouse, sparrow, etc.) and understand that the required purification act is 'nazh' (drawing water from the well).
2
Determine the default number of buckets
Extract the range of 20 to 30 buckets, noting that the number is not fixed but depends on the size of the bucket used.
The range accounts for bucket size: larger bucket means fewer buckets, smaller bucket means more.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that some Hanafi scholars consider 20 buckets wajib and the remaining 10 mustahabb, though the relied-upon position is the full range.
This difference does not affect the practical ruling, as the range is accepted.
4
Recognize the exception for bloated animals
Understand that if the dead animal is bloated or decayed, the entire well must be emptied, as indicated by the hadith interpreted for that condition.
The hadith 'until the water overwhelms you' is applied to the bloated case.

This passage provides a ruling on the purification of a well when a small animal dies in it. The number of buckets to be drawn ranges from twenty to thirty, adjusted for the size of the bucket. The author notes that if the animal is bloated or decayed, the entire well must be emptied. Ruling, specification of bucket count, and evidence.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
For a medium-sized animal in a well, draw forty to fifty buckets — a range based on a mursal hadith.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a small to medium animal falls into a well and dies. The Hanafi school provides a specific number of buckets to draw to restore the water's purity. Understanding the basis and the range is essential for correct application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals classified as medium-sized

Hanafi Ruling: Full Well Emptying for Large Animals
Ruling on large animals requiring full well emptying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for purification of a well when a large animal dies and explain the evidence from the hadith of Zamzam.

Core Idea
A large animal's death in a well requires emptying all water — the impurity is immediate and extensive.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a large animal falls into a well and dies. The Hanafi school prescribes a strict purification — emptying the entire well. We will examine the ruling, its basis in prophetic practice, and how it differs from the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Find the hukm (legal classification) for a well when a dog, sheep, or human dies in it. The text states the entire water must be removed.
The animals listed are considered 'large' in this context.
2
Locate the Dalil
Identify the proof cited: the incident of Zamzam well (an Ethiopian died and the well was emptied) and the narration from Ata' about a dog.
The dalil is a hadith ahad (solitary narration) with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the proof supports the ruling. The command 'akhrij minha' (take it out) implies removal of the water to access the animal, indicating full emptying.
The reasoning connects the action of the Companions to the obligation of complete removal.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that if the water is two qullat or more, it does not become impure unless one of the three qualities (color, taste, smell) changes. Their proof is the hadith of qullatain.
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The Hanafi position (full emptying) is mufta bihi, based on the explicit practice from Zamzam and the size-based analogy. The Shafi'i position relies on a quantitative measure (qullatain) which is not accepted by Hanafis for large impurities.
The tarjih authority is the zahir al-riwayah as recorded by Imam Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۰) وان مات فيها كلب او شاة او نا پاک ہو جائے گا۔ فائی امام شافعی کا مسلک گذر گیا ہے کہ دو مٹکے کنویں میں پانی ہو تو جب تک اوصاف ثلاثہ میں سے ایک نہ بدلے ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ دلیل حدیث قلتین گزرگئی۔ ان نزح : پانی کا کنواں سے نکالنا۔ (۵۰) اور اگر کنویں میں کتا یا بکری یا آدمی مر جائے تو تمام پانی نکالا جائے۔ (۱) یہ جانور بڑے ہوتے ہیں اس کے مرتے ہی پورے کنویں میں نجاست پھیل جائے گی اس لئے پورے کنویں کا پانی نکالا جائے گا (۲) او پر حدیث گزری کہ زمزم کے کنویں میں حبشی مراتو پورا کنواں نکالا گیا (۳) عن عطاء قال اذا سقط الكلب في البئر فاخرج منها حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت علیؓ سے روایت ہے کہ جب کنویں میں چوہا یا جانور گر جائے تو اس کو اتنا نکالو کہ پانی تم پر غالب آجائے (ب) فعمی سے منقول ہے کہ: پرندہ، بلی اور اس مقدار کے جانور کنویں میں گر جائیں تو کنویں سے چالیس ڈول نکالے جائیں گے۔ ایک قول ہے کہ ستر ڈول نکالے جائیں گے۔
And if a dog, sheep, or human dies in it, the entire well becomes impure. ... For the Shafi'i school, if there are two large pots of water, it does not become impure unless one of the three qualities changes... And if a dog, sheep, or human dies in it, all the water must be drawn out.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling for large animals. When a dog, sheep, or human dies in a well, the entire well must be emptied because the large body immediately spreads impurity throughout the water. The commentator also references the Shafi'i position (using the qullatain hadith) and notes a narration from Ata' about a dog. The key principle is that large animals necessitate complete emptying.

Key Terms
نزح جميع ما فيها (nazh jami' ma fiha): Emptying all the water from the well

Key Takeaway
A large animal (dog, sheep, human) dying in a well requires full emptying of all water because the impurity is immediate and extensive, based on the practice of the Companions at Zamzam and the narration from Ata'.

Well Purification: Bloated or Decayed Animals
Ruling when animal is bloated or decayed in the well

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for well purification when a dead animal is bloated or decayed, and explain why size is irrelevant.

Core Idea
Bloating or decay spreads impurity throughout the well, making full emptying wajib regardless of animal size.

Previously, you learned that a small dead animal (like a mouse) that falls into a well and is removed without decomposition requires only partial water removal (e.g., 20-30 buckets). However, if that same animal bloats or decays, the impurity disperses throughout the entire well. This lesson clarifies that size becomes irrelevant—even a tiny sparrow if bloated necessitates complete emptying.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering condition
Read the text carefully. The ruling is activated by two conditions: either the animal becomes bloated (intafakha) or it decays/falls apart (tafasakha). Mere death without these conditions does not trigger this ruling.
These conditions indicate that impurity has spread beyond the immediate area.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is clear: 'nazih jami' ma fiha'—draw all the water in it. This means the entire well must be emptied.
Complete removal of water is wajib.
3
Note the size independence
The text explicitly says 'saghura al-hayawanu aw kabura'—whether the animal is small or large. Size does not affect the ruling because bloating/decay makes the entire water mass impure.
Even a small mouse if bloated requires full emptying.
4
Understand the rationale
The commentator explains that bloating/disintegration spreads impurity (najasa) throughout the whole well. Since water is fluid, the contamination is uniform.
The well's contents are considered a single connected mass.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a well into which a cat falls and dies. If it is removed quickly, partial removal suffices. But if it is left until bloated, the entire well must be emptied.
Time and decomposition are key factors.

The commentator emphasizes that even a small mouse, if bloated, requires complete emptying, citing the saying of Ali (ra).

Well Purification: Standard Bucket Size
Definition of the standard bucket for counting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of the medium bucket (al-dalw al-wasat) and explain why the Hanafi school uses it as the standard for well purification.

Core Idea
The medium bucket (al-dalw al-wasat) is the Shariah standard for counting buckets in well purification, based on the Quranic principle of using the average.

In Hanafi fiqh, when purifying a well that has been contaminated, one must draw a specific number of buckets to remove the impurity. But what counts as a 'bucket'? This passage clarifies that the measure is not any bucket, but the medium-sized bucket commonly used in towns. This ruling is derived from the general Shariah principle of adopting the middle course, as indicated in the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and standard
Recognize that the ruling concerns the purification of a well by drawing water. The standard used to count the buckets is defined here.
2
Understand the definition of al-dalw al-wasat
The standard bucket is the medium-sized bucket (al-dalw al-wasat) commonly used for wells in towns. It holds approximately three and a half kilograms of water.
This is a concrete measure, not abstract.
3
Recognize the evidence from Quran
The commentator cites the Quranic verse (5:89) on kaffarah, where 'awsat' (average) is commanded. This establishes a general principle in Shariah to adopt the average.
The verse is used as a proof (dalil) for this ruling.
4
Apply the principle to well purification
Using the medium bucket, one must draw 40 to 50 buckets to purify the well. The number is tied to this specific bucket size.
If a different bucket size is used, the count would need adjustment to achieve the same volume.
5
Note the consistency of the principle
The principle of using the average is applied consistently across Shariah, as seen in the Quranic command. This ensures fairness and ease.
The Hanafi school relies on this principle for several rulings.

Well Purification: Using a Larger Bucket
Ruling on using a larger bucket than the standard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the number of large bucket draws required to purify a well by applying the proportional counting rule.

Core Idea
When using a larger bucket, count it as its equivalent in medium buckets to achieve the required purification.

This passage addresses a practical question: if a well requires a specific number of medium buckets of water to be drawn for purification, what happens when a larger bucket is used? The ruling provides a clear proportional counting method, ensuring the objective is met without unnecessary hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is drawing water from a well using a bucket larger than the standard medium bucket. The ruling is that it is permissible and the large bucket is counted proportionally.
The ruling is based on achieving the objective (maqsud) rather than the exact count of buckets.
2
Understand the proportional rule
One large bucket is considered equivalent to its capacity in medium buckets. For example, if a large bucket holds 10 medium buckets, drawing one large bucket counts as 10 medium buckets.
3
Apply the rule to a calculation
To find how many large buckets are needed, divide the required number of medium buckets by the capacity of the large bucket. For example, if 20 medium buckets are required and the large bucket holds 10, then 20/10 = 2 large buckets suffice.
This works only if the large bucket's capacity is exactly a multiple of the medium bucket. If not, remainders must be handled? The text does not discuss non-integer ratios, but the principle of proportional counting implies rounding up or using a fractional count? Actually, implicitly the count is exactly proportional; if not a multiple, one may need to supplement with smaller buckets.
4
Recognize the underlying principle
The objective is to remove the required volume of water, not necessarily the exact number of medium buckets. The ruling facilitates ease and practicality.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle of considering intentions and outcomes (al-umur bi-maqasidiha).

Purifying a Spring Well That Cannot Be Emptied
Ruling for a spring well that cannot be emptied

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for purifying a spring well that cannot be emptied and explain the procedure of estimation by two experts.

Core Idea
A spring well that cannot be emptied is purified by drawing out the estimated amount of water present when the impurity fell in.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: a well with a continuous spring that makes complete emptying impossible. The Hanafi school provides a practical solution based on estimation by two experts. Understanding this ruling ensures that the obligation of purification is fulfilled without undue hardship and that the water remains usable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the well type and problem
Determine that the well is a spring well (mu'ayyan) and that the water cannot be entirely removed because of the continuous flow.
This is the key condition triggering the special ruling.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) to draw out the amount of water that was present in the well at the moment the impurity fell in.
This is derived from the hadith cited in the text.
3
Explain the estimation procedure
Two trustworthy and experienced individuals estimate the number of buckets of water in the well at the time of impurity. That exact amount must be drawn out.
The estimation is based on visual assessment and experience.
4
Recognize the basis of the ruling
The ruling relies on a narration from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, which provides the method for such wells.
This is a nawadir authority, but sufficient for practical fatwa.
5
Apply to a scenario
Imagine a spring well with an estimated 30 buckets of water when a dead rat falls in. You must draw out exactly 30 buckets (or the amount agreed by experts).
Drawing more is unnecessary; drawing less may leave impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۴) وان كانت البئر معينا لا ينزح ووجب نزح ما فيها اخرجو مقدار ما فيها من الماء . حين سقط نزع منها عشرون دلوا فان اخرج حين مات نزع منها ستون دلوااو سبعون دلوا فان تفسخ فيها نزح منهاماء ها فان لم تستطيعوا نزح مائة دلو و عشرون و مائة (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب البئر تقع فيه الدابة ج اول ص ۸۲ نمبر ۱۲۷۴ مصنف ابن ابی هیبتة ، ۱۹۸ فی الفارة تقع في البئر ۱۴۹ نمبر ۱۷۱۴) (۵۴) اگر کنواں چشمہ دار ہو کہ پورا پانی نہیں نکالا جاسکتا ہو تو واجب ہے اتنا نکالنا جتنی مقدار اس میں پانی ہے۔ کنویں کے اندر چشمہ جاری ہے اور اتنا پانی نکلتا رہتا ہے کہ سب پانی نکالنا مشکل ہے۔ ایسی صورت میں دو ماہر اور تجربہ کار آدمی سے اندازہ کروایا جائے کہ کنویں میں اس وقت کتنے ڈول پانی ہیں۔ جتنے ڈول اس وقت پانی ہو اتنے ڈول نکال دینے سے کنواں پاک ہو جائے
And if the well is a spring (flowing) that cannot be completely emptied, it is obligatory to draw out the amount of water that is in it.

Commentary
This passage deals with a well that has a spring, so the water cannot be fully emptied. In such a case, it is wajib to estimate the amount of water present at the time the impurity fell in and draw that amount. Two expert and experienced individuals should estimate the number of buckets of water in the well at that moment. Drawing that amount purifies the well.

Key Terms

Standard for Counting Buckets When Emptying a Well
Ruling on measurement standard for well purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the standard for counting buckets when purifying a well and explain the legal basis for using the average bucket.

Core Idea
The average-sized bucket is the legal standard because Shariah consistently takes the middle ground.

When purifying a well, the number of buckets drawn matters. But not all buckets are the same size. This lesson establishes the legal standard: the average bucket used in the locality. This principle is rooted in Quranic guidance to adopt the moderate path, as seen in the kaffarah of feeding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is purifying a well by drawing water. The ruling states that the number of buckets is counted based on the medium bucket used in towns.
This is a wajib standard; deviation may affect the validity of purification.
2
Understand the standard
The 'medium bucket' (al-dalw al-awsat) refers to the bucket of average size commonly used for wells in that area.
If buckets vary, this standard ensures fairness and consistency.
3
Note the underlying principle
Shariah consistently considers the average, as in Quran 5:89 about feeding from the average of what you feed your families.
This principle is called al-awsat in fiqh, a form of istihsan.
4
Apply the ruling
If you draw 40 to 50 average-sized buckets, the well is considered pure. Use the average bucket volume to determine equivalent draws for non-standard buckets.
The exact number may vary based on the well size; the average bucket volume is approximately 3.5 kg.
5
Recognize the wisdom
Adopting the average avoids extremes and ensures practical applicability across different communities.
This is a manifestation of the Hanafi reliance on customary practice (urf).

Source Text

Commentary
This ruling establishes the standard for counting buckets used to empty a well. The bucket considered is the average-sized bucket commonly used for wells in towns. The commentary explains that in Islamic law, the average (al-awsat) is always taken into account, as indicated in the Quran about feeding ten poor people from the average of what you feed your families (Surah al-Ma'idah: 89). The average bucket holds approximately 3.5 kilograms of water. If one removes 40 to 50 average buckets, the well becomes pure.

Ruling on Emptying a Spring-Fed Well
Ruling on purifying a continuously flowing well

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for purifying a spring-fed well and explain why only the water present at the time of contamination must be removed.

Core Idea
A spring-fed well cannot be fully emptied; the obligation is limited to the water present at contamination.

In the previous lessons, we covered the general ruling for emptying a well after contamination. This lesson presents an important exception: a well with a continuous spring (mu'ayyan). Since it is impossible to remove all the water when a spring is flowing, the Shari'ah prescribes a practical solution – only the water that was present at the moment of contamination must be removed. This ruling balances purity requirements with the realities of a natural water source.

Guided Path
1
Identify the well type
Determine if the well is 'mu'ayyan' – fed by a continuous spring that makes complete emptying impossible.
The key term 'معينا' indicates a flowing spring.
2
Recognize the impossibility
Understand that with a spring-fed well, you cannot drain all water because more keeps flowing in. This changes the obligation.
Contrast with a standard well where complete removal is possible.
3
State the ruling
The ruling is that it is obligatory (wajib) to remove only the amount of water that was in the well at the time of contamination.
The Arabic says: 'ووجب نزح ما فيها' – it is obligatory to remove what is in it.
4
Explain the method
Two reliable experts estimate the quantity of water present at the time of contamination. That estimated amount must be removed.
This estimation is a practical concession for spring-fed wells.
5
Note the authority
This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifah, and it is the mufta bihi (operative) ruling. There is an intra-madhhab difference with Imam Muhammad, who requires 200-300 buckets.
The next lesson will cover Imam Muhammad's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كانت البئر معينا لا ينزح ووجب نزح ما فيها اخرجو مقدار ما فيها من الماء
And if the well is of flowing water (spring) that cannot be fully emptied, it is obligatory to remove what is in it, so remove the amount of water that is in it.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This ruling deals with a well that has a continuous spring, making it impossible to remove all the water because it keeps flowing. In such a case, it is obligatory to remove only the amount of water that was present in the well at the time of contamination. Two experts estimate the water volume, and whatever that amount is, it must be removed. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifah. The commentary cites the incident of Zamzam where a person fell in, and they could not empty it completely due to the spring, so Abdullah ibn Zubair said it is sufficient to remove what was there.

Key Terms
معينا (mu'ayyanan): a flowing spring; a well with a continuous water source
نزح (nazh): emptying or removing water from a well

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should be done if a well has a continuous spring and cannot be fully emptied?
A) Remove 200-300 buckets
B) Remove all water including spring water
C) Remove only the water present at the time of contamination
D) The well remains impure forever

Key Takeaway
For a spring-fed well, the obligation is to remove only the water present at the time of contamination, not the continuously flowing spring water.

Imam Muhammad's Concession on Well Purification
Imam Muhammad's view on well purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Muhammad's opinion on well purification and distinguish between the wajib (200 buckets) and mustahabb (300 buckets) amounts.

Core Idea
A well is purified by removing 200 buckets (wajib) and up to 300 (mustahabb) per Imam Muhammad's concession.

This lesson examines a specific narration from Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan regarding well purification. While the primary Hanafi position requires removing all water, Imam Muhammad offered a practical concession based on typical well sizes. Understanding this narration helps you appreciate the flexibility within the Hanafi madhhab and the distinction between the main position (zahir al-riwayah) and rare transmissions (nawadir).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is removing water from a well for purification. Imam Muhammad's narration sets the ruling: 200 buckets are wajib (obligatory) and 300 is mustahabb (recommended).
2
Distinguish Between Wajib and Mustahabb
The narration gives a range: 200 to 300. According to the commentary, the lower bound (200) is the required minimum, while the upper bound (300) is a recommended extra to ensure purity.
This distinction is based on the evidence and the practical reality of well sizes in Kufa and Baghdad.
3
Understand the Concession
Imam Muhammad's view is a concession (rukhsah) from the main position of removing all water. It is based on the observation that most wells contain 200-300 buckets, and removing that amount typically removes the impurity.
The main position (Imam Abu Hanifah) is to remove all water to eliminate any trace of impurity.
4
Compare with the Mufta Bihi
The mufta bihi (operative position for fatwa) is still the main view of removing all water, but Imam Muhammad's opinion is accepted as a valid alternative in cases of hardship.
This is because the narration is from the nawadir (rare transmissions), not from the core zahir al-riwayah texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و عن محمد بن الحسن رحمة الله تعالى انه قال ينزح منها مائتا دلوا الى ثلث مائة
And from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan (may Allah's mercy be upon him) that he said: Two hundred to three hundred buckets are removed from it.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This is a narration from Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani regarding the purification of a well. He stated that 200 to 300 buckets should be removed. The commentary explains that this is for ease. Imam Muhammad observed that wells in Baghdad and Kufa typically contained 200-300 buckets of water, so removing that amount suffices. Two hundred is considered obligatory (wajib) and three hundred is recommended (mustahabb). The primary evidence for removing all water is the hadith of the Ethiopian falling into Zamzam, and the hadith forbidding bathing in stagnant water, indicating the entire well becomes impure.

Key Terms
نوادر (nawadir): Rare or non-standard transmissions within the Hanafi school that are not part of the core six books (Zahir al-Riwayah).
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The core, widely transmitted positions of the Hanafi school from Imam Muhammad's six books.
مفتى به (mufta bihi): The operative ruling that is relied upon for giving fatwas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is the obligatory amount to remove from a well?
A) 100 buckets
B) 200 buckets
C) 300 buckets
D) All water

Key Takeaway
Imam Muhammad's 200-300 bucket concession for well purification is a practical alternative to removing all water, with 200 wajib and 300 mustahabb.

Repeating Prayers for Contaminated Well Water
Ruling statement with expansion on condition of dead animal in well water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating prayers when a dead animal is found in well water, and distinguish between the one-day and three-day cases based on the condition of the animal.

Core Idea
A dead animal found in well water without swelling requires repeating one day of prayers.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: well water used for wudu is later found to contain a dead animal. Since the time of contamination is unknown, the Hanafi school applies caution (ihtiyat) to determine how many previous prayers are invalid. The ruling differs based on whether the animal shows signs of swelling or disintegration, indicating earlier contamination.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The well water was used for wudu (or for washing clothes/items). Subsequently, a dead animal (e.g., a mouse) is discovered in the well. The time it fell in is unknown. Two conditions of the animal are considered: not swollen/not disintegrated, or swollen/disintegrated.
The source text only gives the first case; the second is derived from Abu Hanifah’s commentary.
2
Apply the ruling for no swelling
If the animal is not swollen and not disintegrated, it is assumed to have fallen within the last 24 hours. Therefore, all prayers performed during the past day and night with that wudu must be repeated (wajib). Additionally, any items (clothing, vessels) washed with that water must be re-washed.
The phrase 'صلوة يوم و ليلة' means the prayers of one full day and night.
3
Apply the ruling for swelling/disintegration
If the animal is found swollen or disintegrated, the contamination likely occurred earlier. According to Abu Hanifah, prayers of three days and nights must be repeated, and items washed in that water must be re-washed. This is based on the principle that a dead animal takes at least three days to show such signs.
This second case is not in the base text but is added in the commentary (see below).
4
Understand the legal basis
The ruling is based on caution (ihtiyat) to ensure the validity of worship. Since the exact time is unknown, the maximum plausible time period is taken. This is a distinctive Hanafi approach.
Other schools may have different time estimates or may not require repetition if the water is abundant (e.g., reaching two qullas).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا وجد فى البئر فارة او غيرها ولا يدرون متى وقعت ولم تنتفخ ولم تنفسخ اعادوا صلوة يوم و ليلة اذا كانوا توضؤا منها وغسلوا كل شيء اصابه ماء ها وان
And if a mouse or other than it is found in the well and they do not know when it fell, and it has not swollen and not disintegrated, they repeat the prayer of a day and a night if they performed ablution from it, and they wash everything that its water touched. And if
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This ruling addresses cases where a dead animal is found in a well but the time of falling is unknown. If the animal shows no signs of swelling or disintegration, it is assumed it fell within the past 24 hours. Therefore, any prayers performed with wudu from that water during the past day and night must be repeated. Additionally, any clothing or items washed with that water must be re-washed. If the animal is found swollen or disintegrated, the commentary (from Abu Hanifah) says prayers of three days and nights must be repeated, because the contamination likely occurred earlier. The Arabic text's incomplete 'وان' refers to this second case. This is based on the principle of caution (ihtiyat).

Key Terms
فارة (fa'ra): Mouse or rat; representative of any small dead animal found in water.
بئر (bi'r): Well; a water source dug into the ground.
صلوة يوم وليلة (salatu yawmin wa laylatin): Prayer of a day and a night; meaning all obligatory prayers performed during that 24-hour period.
لم تنتفخ ولم تنفسخ (lam tantafikh wa lam tanfasikh): It has not swollen and not disintegrated; signs of fresh death.
اعادوا (a'adu): They repeat (the prayers), indicating obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a dead mouse is found in a well without swelling, how many days of prayers must be repeated if wudu was performed from that water?
A) None
B) One day and night
C) Three days and nights
D) Seven days

Key Takeaway
The condition of a dead animal found in well water (swollen or not) determines how many days of prayers must be repeated: one day if no swelling, three days if swollen.

Swollen Animal in Well: When to Repeat Prayers
Intra-Hanafi dispute on prayer repetition due to uncertain impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on repeating prayers after finding a dead animal in water and explain the basis for Abu Hanifa's view using circumstantial evidence.

Core Idea
Swelling indicates death three days prior – Abu Hanifa presumes impurity and requires repetition.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether prayers performed with water from a well containing a dead animal must be repeated. The key difference lies in how the condition of the animal (swollen or burst) informs the timeline of impurity. Abu Hanifa uses this as circumstantial evidence to determine the probable time of death, while the Sahibayn require certainty. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how the Hanafi school handles uncertainty (shakk) in matters of purity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling: if the animal is swollen or burst, prayers of three days and nights must be repeated.
The swelling is evidence that death occurred about three days prior.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's objection
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that repetition is not required until the exact time of death is known.
They require certainty (yaqin) about the impurity being present in the water at the time of prayer.
3
Analyse the underlying reasoning
Abu Hanifa relies on istihsan (juristic preference) and the general experience that animal carcasses swell within three days. The Sahibayn adhere to the default principle that certainty is not removed by doubt.
4
Determine the operative ruling
Although the text does not explicitly prefer one view, later Hanafi practice often follows Abu Hanifa out of caution (ihtiyat), making the repetition wajib.
The mufta bihi in many later works is Abu Hanifa's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
انتفخت او تفسخت اعادوا صلوة ثلثة ايام ولياليها في قول ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى (۵۸) وقال ابو يوسف و محمد رحمهما الله تعالى ليس عليهم اعادة شيء حتى يتحققوا متى وقعت (۵۹)
If [the animal] swells or bursts, they repeat the prayer of three days and their nights in the statement of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. (58) And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them both, said: There is no repetition of anything upon them until they ascertain when it occurred. (59)
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
Passage type: intra-Hanafi dispute. This is a ruling from the original matn concerning a well where a dead animal is found swollen or burst. The question is whether to repeat prayers performed with water from that well. Abu Hanifa holds that since swelling typically occurs within three days, we presume the animal died three days prior, and thus all prayers during that period are invalid and must be repeated. His position is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and caution (ihtiyat). The two companions (Sahibayn) hold that repetition is not required because the time of death is uncertain, and certainty of impurity is not established. The original ruling is that the water is najis from the moment of discovery, but its past status remains pure due to the principle that certainty is not removed by doubt. This is an important example of how the Hanafi school handles uncertainty and the burden of proof in matters of impurity.

Key Terms
انتفخت او تفسخت (intafakhat aw tafassakhat): Swollen or burst (referring to a dead animal found in water).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why must prayers performed three days before finding a swollen animal in a well be repeated?
A) Because the animal’s swelling proves it fell exactly three days ago.
B) Because swelling typically occurs within three days, so the water was likely najis for that period.
C) Because the Sahibayn also agree on repetition.
D) Because the Quran commands repeating prayers when impurity is discovered.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a dead animal is found swollen in water, Abu Hanifa's view that prayers of the last three days must be repeated is the operative ruling (mufta bihi), due to the strong circumstantial evidence of swelling.

Su'ur of Humans and Halal Animals is Pure
Ruling with proof on su'ur purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the su'ur of humans and halal animals and support it with the two hadith proofs.

Core Idea
The leftover water of humans and halal animals is pure: the flesh determines the saliva.

This ruling establishes a key principle in taharah: the purity of leftover water depends on the nature of the animal. The Hanafi school relies on clear hadith evidence to categorize su'ur as pure for humans and animals whose meat is eaten. We will examine the proofs and understand their legal implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
State the ruling: the su'ur of humans and halal meat animals is pure (tahir). Note that this includes all land animals and birds whose meat is permissible.
The term 'مايؤكل لحمه' means 'what is eaten' i.e., animals with halal meat.
2
Analyse the first hadith (Ibn Abbas)
The Prophet (peace be upon him) gave his leftover drink to Ibn Abbas, and Ibn Abbas declined to give it to Khalid out of reverence. This implicitly demonstrates that human su'ur is pure and esteemed.
The phrase 'ما كنت لاوثر على سورك احدا' shows Ibn Abbas valued the Prophet's su'ur.
3
Analyse the second hadith (al-Bara')
The Prophet explicitly states 'ما اكل لحمه فلا بأس بسوره' – there is no harm in the su'ur of an animal whose meat is eaten. 'لا بأس' indicates permissibility and purity.
This hadith directly covers all halal animals, not just humans.
4
Understand the underlying reasoning (talil)
The saliva originates from flesh; thus the ruling of the flesh applies to the saliva. If the flesh is halal and pure, the saliva is also pure.
This analogy (qiyas) between flesh and saliva strengthens the ruling.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
Water left by a human or a halal animal is pure and can be used for wudu or drinking. This avoids unnecessary avoidance and ensures clarity in daily worship.
Contrast with su'ur of dogs, pigs, and predators which is najis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسور الآدمى ومايؤكل لحمه طاهر . عن ابن عباس قال دخلت مع رسول الله انا و خالد بن الوليد على ميمونة فجاء تنا باناء من لبن فشرب رسول الله وانا على يمينه و خالد على شماله فقال لي الشربة ما الله لك فان شئت اثرت بها خالدا فقلت ما كنت لاوثر على سورك احدا . عن البراء قال قال رسول الله ما اكل لحمه فلا بأس بسوره .
And the leftover water of humans and what is eaten [i.e., animals whose meat is eaten] is pure. From Ibn Abbas: I entered with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and Khalid ibn al-Walid upon Maymunah, and she brought us a vessel of milk. The Messenger of Allah drank, and I was on his right and Khalid on his left. He said to me, 'The drink is for you; if you wish, you may prefer Khalid.' I said, 'I would not prefer anyone over your leftover water.' From al-Bara': The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Whatever [animal] is eaten, there is no harm in its leftover water.'
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
Passage type: ruling with proof. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position that the su'ur (leftover water or saliva) of a human being is pure, as is the su'ur of any animal whose meat is permissible to eat. The reasoning (talil) given in the text is that saliva originates from flesh (lahm), so the ruling of the flesh applies to the saliva: if the flesh is halal and pure, the saliva is pure. Two proofs are cited: (1) The hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave him a drink after drinking himself, and Ibn Abbas declined to give it to another out of reverence for the Prophet’s su'ur. This establishes the purity of human su'ur. (2) The hadith of al-Bara' where the Prophet explicitly states that there is no harm in the su'ur of an animal whose meat is eaten. This covers all halal land animals, birds, etc. The text also notes that many similar hadith exist.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'ur): The leftover water or saliva after drinking; also used for the moisture left in a vessel after an animal drinks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the su'ur of a cow according to this passage?
A) Najis
B) Pure (tahir)
C) Makruh
D) Mubah but not pure

Key Takeaway
The su'ur of humans and halal meat animals is pure, established by explicit hadith and the principle that saliva follows the ruling of the flesh.
