Hanafi Ruling on Su'ur of Dog: Three Washes vs. Seven
Inter-madhhab dispute over dog's su'ur purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on purifying a vessel after a dog drinks from it, explain the proofs, and compare it with the Shafi'i/Maliki position.

Core Idea
Hanafi: three washes suffice for dog's su'ur; seven-wash hadith is recommended, not obligatory.

This passage addresses the purity status of leftover water (su'ur) from dogs, pigs, and predatory animals. The Hanafi school agrees that such su'ur is impure, but there is a notable difference of opinion regarding the number of washes required to purify a vessel after a dog drinks from it. In this lesson, we will examine the Hanafi position and its evidence, and understand why the Shafi'i and Maliki schools differ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Find the hukm for su'ur of dog, pig, and predatory animals. Note that the Hanafi school considers all these impure.
The text begins with 'وسور الكلب والخنزير وسباع البهائم نجس' – the leftover water is najis.
2
Locate the primary proofs
Read the two hadith from Abu Huraira. The first (Bukhari) orders seven washes; the second (Darqutni) orders three washes. Also note the Quranic verse on pig flesh and the hadith forbidding fanged beasts.
The Hanafi school uses the second hadith (three washes) and regards the first as recommended.
3
Map the dispute
Compare the Hanafi position (three washes suffice) with the Shafi'i/Maliki position (seven washes with earth). Identify the key difference: the interpretation of the same hadith.
The opposition uses the seven-wash hadith from Bukhari; Hanafis argue it is abrogated or specific.
4
Understand the Hanafi tarjih
Why does the Hanafi school choose three washes? Because the principle that najasah is removed by elimination (three washes suffice for heavy impurities) and the qawl of Abu Huraira (a companion) overrides the general command.
Istihsan and the practice of the Sahaba support this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسور الكلب والخنزير وسباع البهائم نجس . عن ابي هريرة ان رسول الله قال اذا شرب الكلب في اناء احدكم فليغسله سبعا . عن ابي هريرة قال اذا ولغ الكلب في الاناء فاهرقه ثم اغسله ثلاث مرات . ولحم خنزير فانه رجس . عن ابي ثعلبة ان رسول الله نهى عن اكل كل ذي ناب من السباع .
And the leftover water of the dog, the pig, and predatory animals of beasts is impure. From Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'When a dog drinks from the vessel of any of you, he should wash it seven times.' From Abu Huraira: He said: 'When a dog laps from a vessel, pour it out, then wash it three times.' And the flesh of pig, for it is an abomination. From Abu Tha'laba: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, forbade eating every fanged beast of prey.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
Passage type: inter-madhhab dispute. The text establishes that the su'ur of dog, pig, and all predatory animals (beasts with fangs) is najis (impure). The proof for the dog's su'ur is given with two hadith: one from Bukhari ordering seven washes (which Shafi'i and Maliki follow), and one from Darqutni ordering three washes (which Hanafis follow). The Hanafi position is that three washes suffice, based on the principle that najasah is removed by elimination, and three washes suffice for heavy impurities like feces and urine. The text mentions that Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik require seven washes with earth for dog su'ur. The Hanafi response relies on the qawl (statement) of Abu Huraira that three washes are sufficient, and that the hadith of seven is acted upon for reward but not obligation. For pig, the Quranic verse 'liham khinzir fa innahu rijs' (Surah al-An'am 145) establishes it as najis al-ayn (impure in essence). For predatory beasts, the hadith from Abu Tha'laba forbids eating them, establishing their flesh as najis, and thus their su'ur is also najis by analogy.

Key Terms
سباع البهائم (siba' al-baha'im): Predatory beasts (fanged animals that hunt).
وسور (su'ur): Leftover water after an animal drinks from a vessel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many times must a vessel be washed if a dog drinks from it?
A) Once
B) Three times
C) Seven times, with earth on the first wash
D) It does not become impure

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on the principle of removal by elimination and the qawl of Abu Huraira to determine that three washes suffice for dog su'ur, with the seven-wash hadith regarded as mustahabb.

The Ruling on Cat, Hen, and Domestic Animal Su'ur
Ruling with proof from hadith that cat, hen, and domestic animal su'ur is makruh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cat su'ur, explain the evidence from hadith, and distinguish it from najis.

Core Idea
Cat su'ur is makruh, not najis, due to explicit hadith and the principle of ease.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on the leftover water (su'ur) of cats, hens, and other domestic animals. The text provides hadith proofs that differentiate cat su'ur from that of a dog, and explicitly states that the cat is not impure. This ruling is grounded in the prophetic principle of removing hardship from the community.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the Hanafi ruling: the su'ur of a cat, hen, and similar domestic animals is makruh tanzihi (disliked, not sinful).
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the hadith that differentiates between dog (seven washes) and cat (one wash), and the hadith that explicitly says the cat is not najis.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling: the explicit negation of najasah indicates purity, but the caution of one wash suggests avoidance, leading to makruh.
4
Apply the Principle of Ease
Recognize that the ruling is based on the cat's constant presence (tawwafin), which would cause hardship if its su'ur were najis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسور الهرة والدجاجة . عن ابي هريرة عن النبي قال يغسل الاناء اذا ولغ فيه الكلب سبع مرات اولاهن واخراهن بالتراب واذا ولغت فيه الهرة غسل مرة . عن ابي هريرة قال النبی السور سبع سن الیھتی . ان رسول الله قال انها ليست بنجس انما هي من الطوافين عليكم والطوافات .
And the leftover water of the cat and the hen. From Abu Huraira from the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Wash the vessel when a dog laps from it seven times, the first and last with earth; and when a cat laps from it, wash once.' From Abu Huraira: The Prophet said: '...the cat seven years...'? The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'It is not impure; it is among those who go around you and go around.'
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
Passage type: ruling with proof (though the ruling 'makruh' is derived from the hadith and the difficulty of avoiding cats). The base matn likely states that the su'ur of a cat is makruh tanzihan (disliked, not sinful). The text provides proofs: (1) A hadith from Tirmidhi and Darqutni that differentiates between dog (seven washes) and cat (one wash), indicating that cat su'ur requires some cleaning but is not like dog. (2) Another hadith stating that the cat is not impure because it is among the 'tawwafin' (those that frequently come and go) – meaning they are domestic animals constantly around people, so strict impurity would cause hardship. Therefore, the Hanafi ruling is that cat su'ur is makruh (disliked) but not najis. This is an application of the legal principle of ease (taysir) in the Shariah. The same ruling applies to free-roaming chickens, predatory birds (like hawks), and domestic pests like snakes and mice, as mentioned in the Urdu commentary.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): Disliked (tanzihan). Not sinful, but better to avoid. It does not nullify or forbid the act.

Ruling on Su'ur of Dog, Pig, and Beasts of Prey
States ruling on su'ur of three animals, provides proofs, and engages inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'ur of dog, pig, and beasts of prey, and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i/Maliki position on washing a vessel after a dog drinks.

Core Idea
Dog su'ur is impure but three washes suffice; seven are recommended for extra reward.

This passage addresses the purity status of the leftover water (su'ur) of animals whose meat is not halal — dog, pig, and beasts of prey. The Hanafi school holds that such su'ur is impure (najis), and specifically for dog su'ur, a vessel may be purified by washing three times. This view is contested by Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik, who require seven washes. The passage presents the Hanafi evidence and explains why the seven-wash hadith is understood as recommended rather than obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling for su'ur of dog, pig, and beasts of prey
Read the opening statement: 'The leftover of dog, pig, and beasts of prey is impure.' Note the reasoning: meat is haram, so saliva (and leftover) is impure.
The principle: if meat is haram, the saliva and leftover inherit that impurity.
2
Examine the inter-madhhab dispute on dog su'ur
Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik rely on the hadith commanding seven washes. The Hanafi school responds with a companion's statement (Abu Huraira) commanding three washes, plus qiyas on other thick impurities.
Hanafis do not reject the seven-wash hadith; they interpret it as mustahabb (recommended).
3
Understand the Hanafi proof: companion's statement and qiyas
The hadith from Abu Huraira — 'When a dog drinks, pour out the water then wash it three times' — is taken as a proof that three washes are sufficient. Qiyas is made on feces and urine, which require three washes to remove.
The companion's statement is considered a valid source (qawl sahabi) in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the treatment of the seven-wash hadith
The Hanafis accept the seven-wash hadith as authentic but do not take it as legally binding (wajib). They consider it a recommendation for extra caution and reward.
This shows the Hanafi approach to reconciling apparently conflicting proofs: one is taken as the minimum (wajib), the other as fadilah (merit).
5
Review the rulings for pig and beasts of prey
Pig su'ur is impure because the pig is najis al-ayn (inherently impure) as per Quran 6:145. Beasts of prey su'ur is impure because their meat is haram based on the hadith forbidding fanged predators.
No dispute on these; all schools agree on impurity.

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة (۲۰) وسور الكلب والخنزير وسباع البهائم نجس (٦٠) کتے کا جوٹھا اور سور کا اور پھاڑ کھانے والے جانور کا جوٹھا ناپاک ہے۔ (۱) کتا، سور اور پھاڑ کھانے والے جانور کا گوشت حلال نہیں ہے۔ اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ تھوک گوشت سے پیدا ہوتا ہے تو گوشت حلال نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کا تھوک اور جو ٹھا بھی ناپاک ہے (۲) کتے کا جوٹھانا پاک ہونے کے سلسلے میں یہ حدیث ہے عن ابـی هــيـرة ان رسول الله الله قال اذا شرب الكلب في اناء احدكم فليغسله سبعا (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا شرب الكلب في اناء احد کم فلیغسلہ سبعا، ص ۲۹، نمبر۱۷۲) اس قسم کی احادیث کی بنا پر امام شافعی اور امام مالک کے یہاں کتے کے جو ٹھے میں برتن کو سات مرتبہ دھونے سے پاک ہو گا (۳) ہماری دلیل حضرت ابو ہریرہ کا کا قول ہے عن ابي هريرة قال اذا ولغ الكلب في الاناء فاهر قه ثم اغسله ثلاث مرات (ب) (دار قطنی، باب ولوغ الكلب فی الاناء ج اور ص ۶۶ نمبر ۱۹۳) اس فتوی سے معلوم ہوا کہ کتے کا جوٹھا تین مرتبہ دھونے سے پاک ہو جائے گا (۴) اصل بات یہ ہے کہ ناپا کی زائل ہونے سے برتن پاک ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور اس سے غلیظ نا پا کی پاخانہ اور پیشاب تین مرتبہ دھونے سے زائل ہو جاتی ہے اور برتن پاک ہو جاتا ہے تو جوٹھا بدرجہ اولی پاک ہو جانا چاہئے۔ البتہ حدیث صحیح پر عمل کرتے ہوئے سات مرتبہ دھوئیگا تو ثواب ملے گا۔ سور نجس العین ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھا تو ناپاک ہو گا ہی۔ ولحم خنزير فانه رجس ( آیت ۴۵ ۱ سورۃ الانعام (۶) پھاڑ کھانے والے جانور کا گوشت حلال نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھا بھی ناپاک ہے۔ اس لئے کہ وہ سبیع یعنی درندہ جانور ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے عن ابی ثعلبة ان رسول الله نهى عن اكل كل ذي ناب من السباع (بخاری شریف، باب اکل کل ذی ناب من السباع نمبر ۵۵۳۰)
Book of Purification (20) The leftover of dog, pig, and beasts of prey is impure. (60) The leftover (su'ur) of dog, pig, and beasts of prey is impure. (1) The meat of dog, pig, and beasts of prey is not lawful (halal). And it has passed previously that saliva originates from meat, so when meat is not lawful, its saliva and leftover are also impure. (2) Regarding the leftover of dog being pure, there is this hadith from Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When a dog drinks from the vessel of one of you, let him wash it seven times.' (Bukhari, chapter on when a dog drinks from a vessel, p. 29, no. 172) Based on such hadiths, according to Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik, the vessel becomes pure by washing it seven times after a dog's leftover. (3) Our proof is the saying of Abu Huraira: 'When a dog drinks from a vessel, pour out the water then wash it three times.' (Darqutni, chapter on dog's lapping, vol. p. 66 no. 193) From this fatwa it is known that the leftover of a dog becomes pure after washing three times. (4) The basic principle is that the vessel becomes pure by removal of impurity. And thick impurities like feces and urine are removed by washing three times, so the vessel becomes pure; then the leftover is even more likely to become pure. However, if one acts upon the authentic hadith and washes seven times, he will get reward. The pig is inherently impure (najis al-ayn), so its leftover is impure indeed. 'And the flesh of swine is indeed impure' (Quran 6:145). (6) The meat of beasts of prey is not lawful, therefore their leftover is also impure, because they are predatory animals. The hadith is from Abu Tha'laba that the Messenger of Allah forbade eating every beast of prey with fangs. (Bukhari, chapter on eating every beast of prey with fangs, no. 5530).
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the impurity of the su'ur (leftover) of dogs, pigs, and beasts of prey. The Hanafi position, as stated at the outset, is that their su'ur is najis. The reasoning is that since their meat is haram, the saliva directly from the meat is also impure. The text then addresses a specific dispute with Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik regarding the dog's su'ur: they consider the vessel purified by seven washes based on the hadith of seven washes. The Hanafis counter with a hadith from Abu Huraira (a companion's statement) that commands three washes, and also employ qiyas (analogy) by comparing it to other thick impurities. However, they do not reject the seven-wash hadith; they acknowledge its authenticity and say that one who performs seven washes for extra caution will receive reward, but the legally required minimum is three. For pig, the Quranic verse 'flesh of swine is impure' is cited, and for beasts of prey, a hadith forbids their consumption. Thus the Hanafi position is established by naqli and aqli proofs.

Key Terms
سور (su'ur): The leftover water or liquid remaining in a vessel after an animal drinks from it.
نجس (najis): Impure; the category of impurity that prevents the validity of prayer if it is present on one's body or clothes, and requires washing.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an action that is rewarded but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Once
B) Three times
C) Seven times
D) Four times

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that dog su'ur is najis, and a vessel is purified by three washes; the seven-wash hadith is authentic but interpreted as recommended.

Ruling on the Su'ur of Certain Animals
States that the su'ur of these animals is makruh and gives evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'ur of cats and other domestic animals, explain the evidence, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The cat's leftover is not impure but makruh tanzihi — proof combines two hadith and the principle of ease.

In daily life, we often encounter animals like cats, hens, and birds. Their leftover water or food raises questions of purity. This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri presents the Hanafi ruling on the su'ur (leftover) of certain animals, using hadith evidence and analogical reasoning. We will see how the Hanafi school reaches a nuanced position of makruh tanzihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its hukm level
The passage states that the su'ur of these animals is makruh. In Hanafi law, makruh tanzihi means it is disliked but not sinful or impure.
This is the first step: know what the ruling is.
2
Recognize the qiyas-based default and the reason for leniency
Cats are beasts of prey, so by qiyas (analogy) with other predatory animals, their leftover would be impure. However, because cats live with humans and avoiding them is difficult, shari'ah provides leniency (tashil).
The principle of easing hardship (raf' al-haraj) is applied.
3
Examine the first hadith (command to wash once)
The hadith orders washing the vessel once after a cat drinks, in contrast to seven times for a dog. This indicates some impurity but less severe.
Dalil al-Dalalah: the difference in number shows a graded ruling.
4
Examine the second hadith (cat is not impure)
Another hadith explicitly states the cat is not impure and it is among those that go around you. This suggests essential purity.
This hadith would support pure (tahir) ruling if taken alone.
5
Combine both hadith to derive makruh tanzihi
To reconcile, the Hanafi scholars conclude the cat's su'ur is not impure (based on second hadith) but is not considered absolutely pure due to the command to wash (from first hadith). Thus it is makruh tanzihi.
This is the Hanafi tarjih (preference) of combining evidences.
6
Apply analogy to other animals
The same ruling applies to other domestic animals like snakes and mice, and to birds of prey, by analogy (qiyas) because they also live around people or have similar impurity concerns.
For the hen, the condition of being free-ranging (mukhallat) is key; if the beak is pure, the su'ur is pure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسور الهرة والدجاجة المخلات وسباع الطيور وما يسكن فى البيوت مثل الحية والفارة مكروه (۱) بلی کا جوٹھا (۲) کھلی پھرنے والی مرغی کا جوٹھا (۳) پھاڑ کھانے والے پرندے (۴) اور اور ان جانوروں کا جوٹھا جوگھر میں رہتے ہوں جیسے سانپ اور چوہا مکروہ ہے۔ (1) بلی پھاڑ کھانے والا جانور ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھا نا پاک ہونا چاہئے لیکن یہ گھر میں رہتی ہے اور اس سے بچنا مشکل ہے اس لئے شریعت نے تسہیل دیدی اور اس کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہوا۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة عن النبي الله قال يغسل الاناء اذا ولغ فيه الكلب سبع مرات اولاهن واخراهن بالتراب واذا ولغت فيه الهرة غسل مرة (ج) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی سور الكلب ص ۲۷ نمبر (۹) عن ابي هريرة قال النبی الله السور سبع سن الیھتی ، باب سور النهر و ج اول ص ۲۴۹ ردار قطنی باب سور الهر ة ج اول نمبر ۲۰۲) بلی کے جوٹھے کے بارے میں یہ حدیث بھی ہے۔ ان رسول الله الله قال انها ليست بنجس انما هي من الطوافين عليكم والطوافات (د) (ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی سور الهر، قاص ۲۷ نمبر ۹۲ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب سور الهر ق ص ۱۲ نمبر حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا جب کتا تم میں سے کسی کے برتن میں پی لے تو اس کو سات مرتبہ دھوؤ (ب) آپ نے فرمایا جب کتا برتن میں منہ ڈالے تو پانی انڈیل دو پھر اس کو تین مرتبہ دھوؤ ۔ ( ج ) آپ نے فرمایا کتا برتن میں منہ ڈال دے تو اس کو سات مرتبہ دھوؤ اور شروع اور اخیر میں مٹی سے دھوؤ ۔ اور جب بلی منہ ڈال دے تو ایک مرتبہ دھویا جائیگا۔ (د) آپ نے فرمایا بلی نا پاک نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ تم پر بار بار آنے والیوں میں سے ہے اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بلی کا جھوٹا پاک ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں حدیثوں کو ملانے کی وجہ سے یہ کہتے ہیں کہ بلی کا جوٹھا مکروہ تنزیہی ہے۔ یہی حال گھر میں رہنے والے تمام جانوروں کا ہے۔ کھلی پھرنے والی مرغی نجاست میں منہ ڈالتی رہتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس کے منہ میں نجاست کے گمان کی وجہ سے مکروہ ہے۔ اگر اس کی چونچ بالکل پاک ہو تو اس کا جوٹھا پاک ہے کیونکہ اس کا گوشت کھایا جاتا ہے۔ ت الدجاجة : مرغی - انخلات : جو کھلی پھرتی ہو ۔ سباع الطيور : وہ پرندے جو شکار کر کے کھاتے ہیں۔ الحیۃ : سانپ۔ الفارة چوہا
The leftover of the cat, the free-ranging hen, birds of prey, and what dwells in houses such as snake and mouse is makruh. (1) The leftover of the cat: the cat is a beast of prey, so its leftover should be impure, but because it stays in the house and it is difficult to avoid it, the law provided leniency and its leftover is made makruh. (2) There is a hadith from Abu Huraira from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Wash the vessel when a dog drinks from it seven times, first and last with soil, and when a cat drinks from it, wash it once.' (Tirmidhi) Also there is a hadith reported: 'Indeed it is not impure; it is from those that go around you.' From this hadith it is known that the cat's leftover is pure. Therefore, combining both hadith, they say the cat's leftover is makruh tanzihi. The same is the case for all animals that live in the house. The free-ranging hen frequently puts its beak into impurities, so due to the suspicion of impurity in its beak, its leftover is makruh. If its beak is completely pure, then its leftover is pure, because its flesh is eaten. 'al-dajaja': hen; 'al-mukhallat': free-ranging; 'siba' al-tuyur': birds that hunt and eat; 'al-hayya': snake; 'al-fara': mouse.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that the su'ur of cats, free-ranging hens, birds of prey, and domestic animals like snakes and mice is makruh (disliked), not najis. The reasoning: cats are predatory by nature, so qiyas would suggest impurity, but because they live closely with humans and it is difficult to avoid them, shari'ah provides leniency. The cat's leftover is considered makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). The text supports this with two hadith: one that orders washing the vessel only once after a cat drinks (in contrast to seven times for dog), and another that explicitly states the cat is not impure. By combining these, the Hanafi deduction is that it is not impure, but it is also not absolutely pure, so it is makruh. For the hen, the ruling applies only if it is free-ranging (mukhallat) and likely to have impurity on its beak; if the beak is known to be pure, the leftover is pure because its meat is halal. Birds of prey and domestic snakes/mice are also ruled makruh by analogy.

Key Terms
مكروه تنزيهاً (makruh tanzihi): A disliked action that is not sinful but is better to avoid. In this context, the leftover is makruh tanzihi meaning it is better not to use it but it is not impure.
مخلات (mukhallat): Free-ranging hen that goes out and may ingest impurities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because it is difficult to avoid cats and the evidence is conflicting
C) Because cats eat mice which are impure
D) Because the Prophet forbade cats

Key Takeaway
The cat's su'ur is makruh tanzihi due to combined evidence, and other problematic animals follow by analogy.

The Doubtful Su'ur of Donkey and Mule
States the Hanafi ruling of donkey/mule su'ur as mashkuk and explains the conflicting dalil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies donkey/mule su'ur as mashkuk (doubtful) and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Contradictory textual evidence on donkeys' purity creates a doubt (mashkuk) that neither confirms purity nor impurity.

The Hanafi school faces a unique dilemma: two Sahih hadiths point in opposite directions regarding donkeys. One forbids donkey meat, implying impurity of its fluids. Another shows the Prophet riding a donkey without washing, implying purity. Because both evidences are strong and contradictory, the Hanafi school suspends judgment and rules the su'ur as mashkuk (doubtful) — a special category for unresolved conflicts. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the reasoning, and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) compared to the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting hadiths
Locate the hadith of Jabir (prohibition of donkey meat at Khaybar) and the hadith of Mu'adh (riding behind the Prophet on a donkey). These are the two competing proofs.
Both are from Sahih Bukhari.
2
Trace each proof's implication for su'ur
From the meat prohibition: if meat is not halal, its bodily fluids (saliva, sweat) are impure. From the riding hadith: contact with sweat did not require washing, indicating sweat (and by extension saliva) is pure.
Sweat and saliva both come from the flesh.
3
Recognize the Hanafi response: suspension of judgment
Because both hadiths are sahih and equally weighty, the Hanafi school does not rule for either, instead declaring the su'ur mashkuk (doubtful).
This is a special category between pure and impure.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Imam Shafi'i gives precedence to the riding hadith (or the principle of original purity) and rules it pure. Note the thamarah al-khilaf: for Shafi'i, normal wudu; for Hanafi, when only such water is available, one must combine wudu and tayammum.
The conflict is not resolved in the same way.
5
Apply to the mule by analogy
Mule, being born from a she-donkey, shares the same ruling (mashkuk) because the mother's ruling extends to the offspring.
Mule is not a separate species for this ruling.

(۶۲) وسور الحمار والبغل مشکوک گدھے کا جوٹھا اور خچر کا جوٹھا مشکوک ہے۔ وجه مشکوک ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ گدھے کے گوشت اور پسینے کے سلسلے میں دونوں قسم کے دلائل ہیں ۔ آپ نے گدھے کا گوشت کھانے سے منع فرمایا۔ اور جب گوشت حلال نہیں ہوگا تو اس کا نکلا ہوا تھوک بھی نجس ہوگا۔ اس اعتبار سے گدھے کا جوٹھا نا پاک ہونا چاہئے ۔ لیکن آپ گدھے پر سوار ہوئے ہیں جس کی وجہ سے آپ کے کپڑے پر گدھے کا پسینہ لگا ہوگا اور پسینہ گوشت سے نکلتا ہے اور کسی پسینے کا حکم بھی وہی ہے جو تھوک کا حکم ہے۔ اس لئے اگر پسینہ لگنے سے کپڑا نہیں دھویا اور پسینہ پاک ہے تو اس اعتبار سے تھوک بھی پاک ہونا چاہئے ۔ تو گویا کہ گدھے کے تھوک کے سلسلے میں دونوں قسم کے دلائل ہیں اس لئے گدھے کا جوٹھا مشکوک ہے۔ نجس ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے عـن جـابـر بـن عبد الله قال نهى رسول الله الله يوم خيبر عن لحوم الحمر ورخص في الخيل (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب غزوہ خیبرج ثانی ص ۶۰۶ نمبر ۴۲۱۹) جب گوشت حلال نہیں تو تھوک بھی پاک نہیں ہوگا۔ اور تھوک پاک ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے عن معاذ قال كنت ردف النبى الله على حمار يقال له عفير (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب اسم الفرس و الحمارص ۴۰۰ نمبر ۲۸۵۶) آپ گدھے پر سوار ہوئے تو کپڑے پر پسینہ لگا ہوگا اور پسینہ پاک ہے تو تھوک بھی پاک ہونا چاہئے ۔ ان دونوں قسم کے دلائل کی وجہ سے گدھے کا جوٹھا مشکوک ہے نان امام شافعی کے نزدیک پچھلے دلائل کی وجہ سے گدھے کا جوٹھا پاک ہے۔ البغل : خچر چونکہ گدھی سے پیدا ہوتا ہے اس لئے جو حکم گدھی کے جو ٹھے کا ہوا وہی حکم خچر کا بھی ہوا۔ یعنی اس کا جوٹھا مشکوک ہے۔
(62) The leftover of the donkey and mule is doubtful. The leftover of the donkey and mule is doubtful. The reason for being doubtful is that there are both types of evidence regarding donkey's meat and sweat. The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade eating donkey meat. And when the meat is not halal, then its saliva will also be impure. In that respect, the donkey's leftover should be impure. But the Prophet rode a donkey, which would cause his clothes to be touched by donkey's sweat, and sweat comes from the flesh, and the ruling of sweat is the same as that of saliva. Therefore, if the clothes were not washed due to sweat, and the sweat is pure, then in that respect the saliva should also be pure. So there are both types of evidence regarding donkey's saliva, therefore the donkey's leftover is doubtful. The evidence for impurity: from Jabir ibn Abdullah, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah on the day of Khaybar forbade the meat of donkeys and permitted horses.' (Bukhari) When the meat is not halal, the saliva will not be pure. And the evidence for purity: from Mu'adh, he said: 'I was riding behind the Prophet on a donkey called 'Ufayr.' (Bukhari) The Prophet rode a donkey, so his clothes would have been touched by sweat, and sweat is pure, so saliva should also be pure. Due to both types of evidence, the donkey's leftover is doubtful. But according to Imam Shafi'i, based on the latter evidence, the donkey's leftover is pure. The mule: since it is born from a she-donkey, the same ruling as the donkey's leftover applies; that is, its leftover is doubtful.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage deals with the su'ur of donkey and mule, ruling it as mashkuk (doubtful). The reason is that there is contradictory evidence: one hadith forbids eating donkey meat, implying that the saliva from its meat is impure (since meat is not halal). On the other hand, the Prophet rode a donkey, and it is known that he did not wash his clothes after contact with the donkey's sweat, indicating that sweat is pure. Since sweat and saliva both originate from the flesh, if sweat is pure, saliva should be pure as well. The text presents both proofs: the prohibition of meat for impurity, and the Prophet's riding for purity. Because of this conflict, the ruling is not conclusive; hence it is mashkuk. The text notes that Imam Shafi'i considers the donkey's su'ur as pure, relying on the riding hadith. The mule follows the ruling of its mother (donkey), so it is also doubtful. The practical implication is that one should not confidently use such water for purification unless necessary.

Key Terms
مشکوک (mashkuk): Doubtful; the ruling is uncertain due to conflicting evidence. The water/su'ur is not definitively pure or impure, leading to a special ruling of doing both wudu and tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the su'ur of a donkey considered 'mashkuk' in the Hanafi school?
A) Because there is no evidence about it
B) Because there is conflicting evidence regarding its purity
C) Because it is like dog's su'ur
D) Because the Prophet forbade its meat, so it is impure

Key Takeaway
The su'ur of donkey and mule is mashkuk (doubtful) due to contradictory textual evidence, leading to a special case requiring both wudu and tayammum when only that water is available.
